Utah Code Annotated - Title 23A - Wildlife Resources Act
========================================================

Utah Code Annotated - Title 23A - Chapter 1 - General Provisions
****************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this title:Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1): "Activity regulated under this title" means an act, attempted act, or activity prohibited or regulated under this title or the rules and proclamations promulgated under this title pertaining to protected wildlife including:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(a): fishing;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(b): hunting;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(c): trapping;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(d): taking;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(e): permitting a dog, falcon, or other domesticated animal to take;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(f): transporting;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(g): possessing;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(h): selling;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(i): wasting;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(j): importing;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(k): exporting;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(l): rearing;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(m): keeping;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(n): using as a commercial venture; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(o): releasing to the wild.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(2): 4-37-103 "Aquaculture facility" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(3): 4-37-103 "Aquatic animal" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(4): "Aquatic wildlife" means species of fish, mollusks, crustaceans, aquatic insects, or amphibians.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(5): "Bag limit" means the maximum limit, in number or amount, of protected wildlife that one person may legally take during one day.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(6): "Big game" means species of hoofed protected wildlife.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(7): "Carcass" means the dead body of an animal or the animal's parts.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(8): "Certificate of registration" means a paper-based or electronic document issued under this title, or a rule or proclamation of the Wildlife Board granting authority to engage in activities not covered by a license, permit, or tag.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(9): "Closed season" means the period of time during which the taking of protected wildlife is prohibited.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(10): "Conservation officer" means a full-time, permanent employee of the division who is POST certified as a peace or a special function officer.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(11): "Dedicated hunter program" means a program that provides:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(11)(a): expanded hunting opportunities;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(11)(b): opportunities to participate in projects that are beneficial to wildlife; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(11)(c): education in hunter ethics and wildlife management principles.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(12): "Department" means the Department of Natural Resources.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(13): 23A-2-202 "Director" means the director of the division appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(14): "Division" means the Division of Wildlife Resources.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(15): 23A-1-103 Subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(15)(a): where an individual has a fixed permanent home and principal establishment;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(15)(b): to which the individual if absent, intends to return and has an actual plan, method, and means to return to the individual's domicile within six months;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(15)(c): in which the individual, and the individual's family voluntarily reside, not for a special or temporary purpose, but with the intention of making a permanent home; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(15)(d): is a place where the individual resides for the majority of the individual's time.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(16): "Endangered" means wildlife designated as endangered according to Section 3 of the federal Endangered Species Act of 1973.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(17): "Executive director" means the executive director of the Department of Natural Resources.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(18): 4-37-103 "Fee fishing facility" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(19): "Feral" means an animal that is normally domesticated but has reverted to the wild.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(20): "Fishing" means to take fish or crayfish by any means.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(21): "Furbearer" means species of the Bassariscidae, Canidae, Felidae, Mustelidae, and Castoridae families, except coyote and cougar.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(22): "Game" means wildlife normally pursued, caught, or taken by sporting means for human use.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(23): "Hunting" means to take or pursue a reptile, amphibian, bird, or mammal by any means.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(24): 58-79-102 "Hunting guide" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(25): "Intimidate or harass" means to physically interfere with or impede, hinder, or diminish the efforts of an officer in the performance of the officer's duty.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(26): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(26)(a): "Natural flowing stream" means a topographic low where water collects and perennially or intermittently flows with a perceptible current in a channel formed exclusively by forces of nature.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(26)(b): "Natural flowing stream" includes perennial or intermittent water flows in a:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(26)(b)(i): realigned or modified channel that replaces the historic, natural flowing stream channel; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(26)(b)(ii): dredged natural flowing stream channel.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(26)(c): "Natural flowing stream" does not include a human-made ditch, canal, pipeline, or other water delivery system that diverts and conveys water to an approved place of use pursuant to a certificated water right.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(27): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(27)(a): "Natural lake" means a perennial or intermittent body of water that collects on the surface of the earth exclusively through the forces of nature and without human assistance.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(27)(b): "Natural lake" does not mean a lake where the surface water sources supplying the body of water originate from groundwater springs no more than 100 yards upstream.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(28): 23A-2-302 "Nominating committee" means the Wildlife Board Nominating Committee created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(29): "Nonresident" means a person who does not qualify as a resident.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(30): "Open season" means the period of time during which protected wildlife may be legally taken.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(31): 58-79-102 "Outfitter" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(32): "Pecuniary gain" means the acquisition of money or something of monetary value.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(33): "Permit" means a paper-based or electronic document that grants authority to engage in specified activities under this title or a rule or proclamation of the Wildlife Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(34): "Person" means an individual, association, partnership, government agency, corporation, or an agent of the individual, association, partnership, government agency, or corporation.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(35): "Pollute water" means to introduce into waters within the state matter or thermal energy that:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(35)(a): exceeds state water quality standards; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(35)(b): could harm protected wildlife.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(36): "Possession" means actual or constructive possession.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(37): "Possession limit" means the number of bag limits one individual may legally possess.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(38): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(38)(a): "Private fish pond" means a pond, reservoir, or other body of water, including a fish culture system, located on privately owned land where privately owned fish:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(38)(a)(i): are propagated or kept for a private noncommercial purpose; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(38)(a)(ii): may be taken without a fishing license.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(38)(b): "Private fish pond" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(38)(b)(i): an aquaculture facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(38)(b)(ii): a fee fishing facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(38)(b)(iii): a short-term fishing event; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(38)(b)(iv): private stocking.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(39): 23A-9-203 "Private stocking" means an authorized release of privately owned, live fish in the waters of the state not eligible as:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(39)(a): 23A-9-203 a private fish pond under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(39)(b): an aquaculture facility or fee fishing facility under Title 4, Chapter 37, Aquaculture Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(40): "Private wildlife farm" means an enclosed place where privately owned birds or furbearers are propagated or kept and that restricts the birds or furbearers from:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(40)(a): commingling with wild birds or furbearers; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(40)(b): escaping into the wild.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(41): "Proclamation" means the publication that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(41)(a): used to convey a statute, rule, policy, or pertinent information related to wildlife; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(41)(b): issued in accordance with a rule made by the Wildlife Board under this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(42): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(42)(a): "Protected aquatic wildlife" means aquatic wildlife except as provided in Subsection (42)(b).
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(42)(b): "Protected aquatic wildlife" does not include aquatic insects.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(43): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(43)(a): "Protected wildlife" means wildlife, except as provided in Subsection (43)(b).
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(43)(b): "Protected wildlife" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(43)(b)(i): coyote;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(43)(b)(ii): field mouse;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(43)(b)(iii): gopher;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(43)(b)(iv): ground squirrel;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(43)(b)(v): jack rabbit;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(43)(b)(vi): muskrat; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(43)(b)(vii): raccoon.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(44): 23A-2-303 "Regional advisory council" means a council created under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(45): "Released to the wild" means to be turned loose from confinement.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(46): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(46)(a): "Reservoir constructed on a natural stream channel" means a body of water collected and stored on the course of a natural flowing stream by impounding the stream through excavation or diking.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(46)(b): "Reservoir constructed on a natural stream channel" does not mean an impoundment on a natural flowing stream where all surface water sources supplying the impoundment originate from groundwater springs no more than 100 yards upstream.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(47): 23A-1-103 Subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(47)(a): has been domiciled in the state for six consecutive months immediately preceding the purchase of a license; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(47)(b): does not claim residency for hunting, fishing, or trapping in another state or country.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(48): "Sell" means to offer or possess for sale, barter, exchange, or trade, or the act of selling, bartering, exchanging, or trading.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(49): "Short-term fishing event" means an event when:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(49)(a): privately acquired fish are held or confined for a period not to exceed 10 days for the purpose of providing fishing or recreational opportunity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(49)(b): no fee is charged as a requirement to fish.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(50): "Small game" means species of protected wildlife:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(50)(a): commonly pursued for sporting purposes;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(50)(b): not classified as big game, aquatic wildlife, or furbearers; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(50)(c): excluding turkey, cougar, and bear.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(51): "Spoiled" means impairment of the flesh of wildlife that renders the flesh unfit for human consumption.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(52): "Spotlighting" means throwing or casting the rays of a spotlight, headlight, or other artificial light on a highway or in a field, woodland, or forest while having in possession a weapon by which protected wildlife may be killed.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(53): "Tag" means a card, label, or other paper-based or electronic means of identification used to document harvest of protected wildlife.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(54): "Take" means to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(54)(a): hunt, pursue, harass, catch, capture, possess, gather, angle, seine, trap, or kill protected wildlife; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(54)(b): attempt an action referred to in Subsection (54)(a).
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(55): "Threatened" means wildlife designated as threatened pursuant to Section 3 of the federal Endangered Species Act of 1973.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(56): "Trapping" means taking protected wildlife with a trapping device.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(57): "Trophy animal" means an animal described as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(57)(a): deer - a buck with an outside antler measurement of 24 inches or greater;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(57)(b): elk - a bull with six points on at least one side;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(57)(c): bighorn, desert, or rocky mountain sheep - a ram with a curl exceeding half curl;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(57)(d): moose - a bull with at least one antler exceeding five inches in length;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(57)(e): mountain goat - a male or female;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(57)(f): pronghorn antelope - a buck with horns exceeding 14 inches; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(57)(g): bison - a bull.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(58): "Upland game" means pheasant, quail, partridge, grouse, ptarmigan, mourning dove, band-tailed pigeon, turkey, cottontail rabbit, or snowshoe hare.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(59): "Waste" means to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(59)(a): abandon protected wildlife; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(59)(b): allow protected wildlife to spoil or to be used in a manner not normally associated with the protected wildlife's beneficial use.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(60): "Wild" means the natural environment, including a private pond or private property.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(61): "Wildlife" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(61)(a): crustaceans, including brine shrimp and crayfish;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(61)(b): mollusks; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(61)(c): vertebrate animals living in nature, except feral animals.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(62): 23A-2-301 "Wildlife Board" means the board created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(63): "Wildlife parts" means biological material derived from the body or anatomy of wildlife, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(63)(a): an antler or horn;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(63)(b): a hide;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(63)(c): a bone; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(63)(d): meat.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this title:Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1): "Activity regulated under this title" means an act, attempted act, or activity prohibited or regulated under this title or the rules and proclamations promulgated under this title pertaining to protected wildlife including:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(a): fishing;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(b): hunting;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(c): trapping;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(d): taking;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(e): permitting a dog, falcon, or other domesticated animal to take;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(f): transporting;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(g): possessing;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(h): selling;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(i): wasting;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(j): importing;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(k): exporting;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(l): rearing;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(m): keeping;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(n): using as a commercial venture; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(1)(o): releasing to the wild.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(2): 4-37-103 "Aquaculture facility" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(3): 4-37-103 "Aquatic animal" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(4): "Aquatic wildlife" means species of fish, mollusks, crustaceans, aquatic insects, or amphibians.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(5): "Bag limit" means the maximum limit, in number or amount, of protected wildlife that one person may legally take during one day.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(6): "Big game" means species of hoofed protected wildlife.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(7): "Carcass" means the dead body of an animal or the animal's parts.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(8): "Certificate of registration" means a paper-based or electronic document issued under this title, or a rule or proclamation of the Wildlife Board granting authority to engage in activities not covered by a license, permit, or tag.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(9): "Closed season" means the period of time during which the taking of protected wildlife is prohibited.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(10): "Dedicated hunter program" means a program that provides:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(10)(a): expanded hunting opportunities;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(10)(b): opportunities to participate in projects that are beneficial to wildlife; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(10)(c): education in hunter ethics and wildlife management principles.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(11): "Department" means the Department of Natural Resources.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(12): 23A-2-202 "Director" means the director of the division appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(13): "Division" means the Division of Wildlife Resources.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(14): "Division of Law Enforcement" means the division within the Department of Natural Resources created under Title 79, Chapter 2, Part 7, Division of Law Enforcement.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(15): 23A-1-103 Subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(15)(a): where an individual has a fixed permanent home and principal establishment;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(15)(b): to which the individual if absent, intends to return and has an actual plan, method, and means to return to the individual's domicile within six months;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(15)(c): in which the individual, and the individual's family voluntarily reside, not for a special or temporary purpose, but with the intention of making a permanent home; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(15)(d): is a place where the individual resides for the majority of the individual's time.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(16): "Endangered" means wildlife designated as endangered according to Section 3 of the federal Endangered Species Act of 1973.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(17): "Executive director" means the executive director of the Department of Natural Resources.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(18): 4-37-103 "Fee fishing facility" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(19): "Feral" means an animal that is normally domesticated but has reverted to the wild.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(20): "Fishing" means to take fish or crayfish by any means.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(21): "Furbearer" means species of the Bassariscidae, Canidae, Felidae, Mustelidae, and Castoridae families, except coyote and cougar.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(22): "Game" means wildlife normally pursued, caught, or taken by sporting means for human use.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(23): "Hunting" means to take or pursue a reptile, amphibian, bird, or mammal by any means.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(24): 58-79-102 "Hunting guide" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(25): "Intimidate or harass" means to physically interfere with or impede, hinder, or diminish the efforts of an officer in the performance of the officer's duty.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(26): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(26)(a): "Natural flowing stream" means a topographic low where water collects and perennially or intermittently flows with a perceptible current in a channel formed exclusively by forces of nature.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(26)(b): "Natural flowing stream" includes perennial or intermittent water flows in a:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(26)(b)(i): realigned or modified channel that replaces the historic, natural flowing stream channel; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(26)(b)(ii): dredged natural flowing stream channel.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(26)(c): "Natural flowing stream" does not include a human-made ditch, canal, pipeline, or other water delivery system that diverts and conveys water to an approved place of use pursuant to a certificated water right.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(27): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(27)(a): "Natural lake" means a perennial or intermittent body of water that collects on the surface of the earth exclusively through the forces of nature and without human assistance.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(27)(b): "Natural lake" does not mean a lake where the surface water sources supplying the body of water originate from groundwater springs no more than 100 yards upstream.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(28): 79-2-701 "Natural resources officer" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(29): 23A-2-302 "Nominating committee" means the Wildlife Board Nominating Committee created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(30): "Nonresident" means a person who does not qualify as a resident.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(31): "Open season" means the period of time during which protected wildlife may be legally taken.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(32): 58-79-102 "Outfitter" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(33): "Pecuniary gain" means the acquisition of money or something of monetary value.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(34): "Permit" means a paper-based or electronic document that grants authority to engage in specified activities under this title or a rule or proclamation of the Wildlife Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(35): "Person" means an individual, association, partnership, government agency, corporation, or an agent of the individual, association, partnership, government agency, or corporation.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(36): "Pollute water" means to introduce into waters within the state matter or thermal energy that:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(36)(a): exceeds state water quality standards; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(36)(b): could harm protected wildlife.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(37): "Possession" means actual or constructive possession.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(38): "Possession limit" means the number of bag limits one individual may legally possess.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(39): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(39)(a): "Private fish pond" means a pond, reservoir, or other body of water, including a fish culture system, located on privately owned land where privately owned fish:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(39)(a)(i): are propagated or kept for a private noncommercial purpose; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(39)(a)(ii): may be taken without a fishing license.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(39)(b): "Private fish pond" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(39)(b)(i): an aquaculture facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(39)(b)(ii): a fee fishing facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(39)(b)(iii): a short-term fishing event; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(39)(b)(iv): private stocking.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(40): 23A-9-203 "Private stocking" means an authorized release of privately owned, live fish in the waters of the state not eligible as:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(40)(a): 23A-9-203 a private fish pond under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(40)(b): an aquaculture facility or fee fishing facility under Title 4, Chapter 37, Aquaculture Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(41): "Private wildlife farm" means an enclosed place where privately owned birds or furbearers are propagated or kept and that restricts the birds or furbearers from:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(41)(a): commingling with wild birds or furbearers; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(41)(b): escaping into the wild.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(42): "Proclamation" means the publication that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(42)(a): used to convey a statute, rule, policy, or pertinent information related to wildlife; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(42)(b): issued in accordance with a rule made by the Wildlife Board under this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(43): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(43)(a): "Protected aquatic wildlife" means aquatic wildlife except as provided in Subsection (43)(b).
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(43)(b): "Protected aquatic wildlife" does not include aquatic insects.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(44): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(44)(a): "Protected wildlife" means wildlife, except as provided in Subsection (44)(b).
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(44)(b): "Protected wildlife" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(44)(b)(i): coyote;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(44)(b)(ii): field mouse;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(44)(b)(iii): gopher;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(44)(b)(iv): ground squirrel;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(44)(b)(v): jack rabbit;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(44)(b)(vi): muskrat; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(44)(b)(vii): raccoon.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(45): 23A-2-303 "Regional advisory council" means a council created under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(46): "Released to the wild" means to be turned loose from confinement.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(47): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(47)(a): "Reservoir constructed on a natural stream channel" means a body of water collected and stored on the course of a natural flowing stream by impounding the stream through excavation or diking.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(47)(b): "Reservoir constructed on a natural stream channel" does not mean an impoundment on a natural flowing stream where all surface water sources supplying the impoundment originate from groundwater springs no more than 100 yards upstream.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(48): 23A-1-103 Subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(48)(a): has been domiciled in the state for six consecutive months immediately preceding the purchase of a license; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(48)(b): does not claim residency for hunting, fishing, or trapping in another state or country.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(49): "Sell" means to offer or possess for sale, barter, exchange, or trade, or the act of selling, bartering, exchanging, or trading.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(50): "Short-term fishing event" means an event when:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(50)(a): privately acquired fish are held or confined for a period not to exceed 10 days for the purpose of providing fishing or recreational opportunity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(50)(b): no fee is charged as a requirement to fish.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(51): "Small game" means species of protected wildlife:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(51)(a): commonly pursued for sporting purposes;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(51)(b): not classified as big game, aquatic wildlife, or furbearers; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(51)(c): excluding turkey, cougar, and bear.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(52): "Spoiled" means impairment of the flesh of wildlife that renders the flesh unfit for human consumption.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(53): "Spotlighting" means throwing or casting the rays of a spotlight, headlight, or other artificial light on a highway or in a field, woodland, or forest while having in possession a weapon by which protected wildlife may be killed.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(54): "Tag" means a card, label, or other paper-based or electronic means of identification used to document harvest of protected wildlife.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(55): "Take" means to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(55)(a): hunt, pursue, harass, catch, capture, possess, gather, angle, seine, trap, or kill protected wildlife; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(55)(b): attempt an action referred to in Subsection (55)(a).
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(56): "Threatened" means wildlife designated as threatened pursuant to Section 3 of the federal Endangered Species Act of 1973.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(57): "Trapping" means taking protected wildlife with a trapping device.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(58): "Trophy animal" means an animal described as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(58)(a): deer - a buck with an outside antler measurement of 24 inches or greater;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(58)(b): elk - a bull with six points on at least one side;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(58)(c): bighorn, desert, or rocky mountain sheep - a ram with a curl exceeding half curl;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(58)(d): moose - a bull with at least one antler exceeding five inches in length;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(58)(e): mountain goat - a male or female;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(58)(f): pronghorn antelope - a buck with horns exceeding 14 inches; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(58)(g): bison - a bull.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(59): "Upland game" means pheasant, quail, partridge, grouse, ptarmigan, mourning dove, band-tailed pigeon, turkey, cottontail rabbit, or snowshoe hare.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(60): "Waste" means to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(60)(a): abandon protected wildlife; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(60)(b): allow protected wildlife to spoil or to be used in a manner not normally associated with the protected wildlife's beneficial use.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(61): "Wild" means the natural environment, including a private pond or private property.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(62): "Wildlife" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(62)(a): crustaceans, including brine shrimp and crayfish;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(62)(b): mollusks; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(62)(c): vertebrate animals living in nature, except feral animals.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(63): 23A-2-301 "Wildlife Board" means the board created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(64): "Wildlife parts" means biological material derived from the body or anatomy of wildlife, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(64)(a): an antler or horn;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(64)(b): a hide;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(64)(c): a bone; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-101(64)(d): meat.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-102 Wildlife declared property of the state.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-102(1): Wildlife existing within this state, not held by private ownership and legally acquired, is the property of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-102(2): Fish released under private stocking become the property of the state and subject to the fishing regulations set forth in this title or a rule or proclamation of the Wildlife Board.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103 Domicile or residency.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(1): 23A-1-101; 23A-1-101
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(1)(a): 23A-1-101; 23A-1-101 Subject to Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(1)(a)(i): has been domiciled in the state for six consecutive months immediately preceding the purchase of a license or application of a license, permit, or tag; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(1)(a)(ii): does not claim residency for hunting, fishing, or trapping in another state or country.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(1)(b): To create a new domicile an individual shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(1)(b)(i): abandon the old domicile; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(1)(b)(ii): be able to prove that a new domicile has been established.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(2): 23A-1-101 A Utah resident retains Utah residency if that individual leaves this state:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(2)(a): to serve in the armed forces of the United States or for religious or educational purposes; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(2)(b): 23A-1-101 the individual complies with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(3): 23A-1-101
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(3)(a): 23A-1-101 A member of the armed forces of the United States and dependents are residents for the purposes of this title as of the date the member reports for duty under assigned orders in the state if the member:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(3)(a)(i): is not on temporary duty in this state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(3)(a)(ii): 23A-1-101 complies with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(3)(b): A member shall present a copy of the assignment orders to a division office to verify the member's qualification as a resident.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(4): 23A-1-101 A nonresident attending an institution of higher learning in this state as a full-time student may qualify as a resident for purposes of this title if the student:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(4)(a): has been present in this state for 60 consecutive days immediately preceding the purchase of the license; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(4)(b): 23A-1-101 complies with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(5): A Utah resident license is invalid if a resident license for hunting, fishing, or trapping is purchased in another state or country.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-103(6): An absentee landowner paying property tax on land in Utah does not qualify as a resident.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-201 Private wildlife farms.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-201(1): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-201(1)(a): Subject to the requirements of this section, a person may:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-201(1)(a)(i): establish and maintain a private wildlife farm for propagating, rearing, and keeping furbearers or birds classified as protected wildlife; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-201(1)(a)(ii): sell or dispose of wildlife reared upon the private wildlife farm, except that disposal may not include release to the wild without first securing written permission from the Wildlife Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-201(1)(b): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act Before establishing a private wildlife farm, a person shall obtain written authorization from the division in accordance with rules established by the Wildlife Board in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-201(1)(c): Wildlife that escapes from a private wildlife farm becomes the property of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-201(2): This section does not:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-201(2)(a): apply to a private fur farm established and maintained for rearing domesticated, privately owned mink or chinchilla that were not acquired as wild animals from a state or country; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-201(2)(b): provide for the propagating, rearing, and keeping of a protected wildlife other than a wildlife specified in this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202 Agreement with a tribe.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(1): As used in this section, "tribe" means a federally recognized:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(1)(a): Indian tribe; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(1)(b): Indian band.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2): 23A-4-1110; 23A-11-202
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(a): Subject to the requirements of this section, the governor may enter into an agreement with a tribe to settle a dispute between the state and the tribe concerning a hunting, fishing, or trapping right claim that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(a)(i): based on:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(a)(i)(A): a treaty;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(a)(i)(B): an aboriginal right; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(a)(i)(C): other recognized federal right; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(a)(ii): on lands located within the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(b): Except as provided in Subsection (2)(c), an agreement permitted under Subsection (2)(a) may not exempt a person from the requirements of this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(c): 23A-4-1110; 23A-11-202 An agreement permitted under Subsection (2)(a) may exempt or partially exempt a tribe that is a party to the agreement or a member of that tribe from:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(c)(i): 23A-4-1110 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(c)(ii): 23A-11-202 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(c)(iii): a hunter or furharvester education requirement under Chapter 4, Licenses, Permits, Certificates of Registration, and Tags;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(c)(iv): an age restriction under Chapter 4, Licenses, Permits, Certificates of Registration, and Tags;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(c)(v): paying a fee required under this title to obtain a hunting, fishing, or trapping license or permit;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(c)(vi): obtaining a license or permit required under this title to hunt, trap, or fish; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(c)(vii): complying with a rule or proclamation of the Wildlife Board if the exemption is not inconsistent with this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(d): An agreement permitted under Subsection (2)(a) shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(d)(i): be in writing;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(d)(ii): be signed by:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(d)(ii)(A): the governor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(d)(ii)(B): the governing body of the tribe that:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(d)(ii)(B)(I): is designated by the tribe; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(d)(ii)(B)(II): may bind the tribe to the terms of the agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(d)(iii): be conditioned on obtaining any approval required by federal law;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(d)(iv): state the effective date of the agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(d)(v): provide that the governor shall renegotiate the agreement if the agreement is or becomes inconsistent with a state statute for which an exemption is not authorized under this section; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(d)(vi): include any accommodation made by the tribe that:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(d)(vi)(A): is agreed to by the tribe;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(d)(vi)(B): is reasonably related to the agreement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(d)(vi)(C): concerns the management and use of wildlife resources or habitat.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(e): Before executing an agreement under this Subsection (2), the governor shall consult with:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(e)(i): the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(e)(ii): the chair of the Wildlife Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(f): At least 30 days before the agreement under this Subsection (2) is executed, the governor or the governor's designee shall provide a copy of the agreement in the form that the agreement will be executed to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(f)(i): the chairs of the Native American Legislative Liaison Committee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-202(2)(f)(ii): the Office of Legislative Research and General Counsel.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-203 Utah State Hunting and Fishing Day.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
In recognition of the substantial and continued contribution by hunters and fishermen toward the sound management of wildlife in Utah, the fourth Saturday of September of each year is known as "Utah State Hunting and Fishing Day."

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204 Spotlighting of coyote, red fox, striped skunk, and raccoon -- County ordinances -- Permits.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(1): 41-6a-102 For purposes of a county ordinance enacted pursuant to this section, "motor vehicle" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(2): Spotlighting may be used to hunt coyote, red fox, striped skunk, or raccoon when allowed by a county ordinance enacted pursuant to this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(3): The ordinance shall provide that:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(3)(a): a hunter shall carry the artificial light used to spotlight coyote, red fox, striped skunk, or raccoon;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(3)(b): a motor vehicle headlight or light attached to or powered by a motor vehicle may not be used to spotlight the coyote, red fox, striped skunk, or raccoon; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(3)(c): while hunting with the use of an artificial light, the hunter may not occupy or operate a motor vehicle.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(4): The ordinance may specify:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(4)(a): the time of day and seasons when spotlighting is permitted;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(4)(b): areas closed or open to spotlighting within the unincorporated area of the county;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(4)(c): safety zones within which spotlighting is prohibited;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(4)(d): the weapons permitted; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(4)(e): penalties for violation of the ordinance.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(5)(a): A county may restrict the number of hunters engaging in spotlighting by requiring a permit to spotlight and issuing a limited number of permits.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(5)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(5)(b)(i): A county may charge a fee for a spotlighting permit.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(5)(b)(ii): A county ordinance shall establish the permit fee.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(5)(b)(iii): A county shall remit revenue generated by the permit fee to the division for deposit into the Wildlife Resources Account, except the Wildlife Board may allow a county that enacts an ordinance pursuant to this section to retain a reasonable amount to pay for the costs of administering and enforcing the ordinance if the use of the permit revenues does not affect federal funds received by the state under Wildlife Restoration Act, 16 U.S.C. Sec. 669 et seq., and Sport Fish Restoration Act, 16 U.S.C. Sec. 777 et seq.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(6): A county may require a hunter to notify the county sheriff of the time and place the hunter will be engaged in spotlighting.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(7): The requirement that a county enact an ordinance before a person may use spotlighting to hunt coyote, red fox, striped skunk, or raccoon does not apply to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(7)(a): a person or the person's agent who is lawfully acting to protect the person's crops or domestic animals from predation by those animals; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-204(7)(b): an animal damage control agent acting in the agent's official capacity under a memorandum of agreement with the division.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-205 Donating protected wildlife.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-205(1): A person may only donate protected wildlife or wildlife parts to another person in accordance with this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-205(2): Documentation of donation shall be kept with the protected wildlife or wildlife parts showing:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-205(2)(a): the number and species of protected wildlife or wildlife parts donated;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-205(2)(b): the date of donation;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-205(2)(c): the license or permit number of the donor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-205(2)(d): an image or picture of the wildlife or wildlife parts donated.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-205(3): Notwithstanding Subsections (1) and (2), a person may donate the hide of a big game animal to another person at any place without a donation slip.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-206 New development.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-206(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-206(1)(a): "Mitigate" means an activity intended to lessen known negative impacts caused by wildlife, including relocating or distracting wildlife.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-206(1)(b): "New development" means the conversion in use of previously undeveloped land into a developed state that occurs on or after May 1, 2024.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-206(1)(c): "Wildlife damage or nuisance claim" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-206(1)(c)(i): a depredation claim;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-206(1)(c)(ii): a wildlife damage claim; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-206(1)(c)(iii): a nuisance complaint involving wildlife.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-206(2): On and after May 1, 2024, new development in the state is considered infringing on existing wildlife habitat and a person who makes a wildlife damage or nuisance claim related to the new development may not qualify for a wildlife damage or nuisance claim against the state or a political subdivision.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-1-206(3): Notwithstanding Subsection (2), the division may mitigate wildlife damage or nuisances impacting a new development.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 23A - Chapter 2 - Administration
************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-101 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
Reserved.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-102 Powers of division to determine facts -- Policymaking powers of Wildlife Board.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-102(1): The division may determine the facts relevant to the wildlife resources of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-102(2): 23A-2-303
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-102(2)(a): Upon a determination of the facts, the Wildlife Board shall establish the policies best designed to accomplish the purposes and fulfill the intent of the laws pertaining to wildlife and the preservation, protection, conservation, perpetuation, introduction, and management of wildlife.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-102(2)(b): In establishing policy, the Wildlife Board shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-102(2)(b)(i): recognize that wildlife and the wildlife's habitat are an essential part of a healthy, productive environment;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-102(2)(b)(ii): recognize the impact of wildlife on humans, human economic activities, private property rights, and local economies;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-102(2)(b)(iii): seek to balance the habitat requirements of wildlife with the social and economic activities of humans;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-102(2)(b)(iv): recognize the social and economic values of wildlife, including fishing, hunting, and other uses; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-102(2)(b)(v): seek to maintain wildlife on a sustainable basis.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-102(2)(c): 23A-2-303
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-102(2)(c)(i): 23A-2-303 The Wildlife Board shall consider the recommendations of the regional advisory councils established in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-102(2)(c)(ii): If a regional advisory council recommends a position or action to the Wildlife Board, and the Wildlife Board rejects the recommendation, the Wildlife Board shall provide a written explanation to the regional advisory council recommending the opposing position.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-102(3): An authority conferred upon the Wildlife Board by this title may not supersede the administrative authority of the executive director or the director.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201 Division of Wildlife Resources -- Limits on authority of political subdivisions -- Adjudicative proceedings -- Official seal.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(1)(a): There is created the Division of Wildlife Resources within the Department of Natural Resources under the administration and general supervision of the executive director.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(1)(b): The division is the wildlife authority for Utah and is vested with the functions, powers, duties, rights, and responsibilities provided in this title and other law.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(2)(a): Subject to the broad policymaking authority of the Wildlife Board, the division shall protect, propagate, manage, conserve, and distribute protected wildlife throughout the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(2)(b): The division is the trustee and custodian of protected wildlife and may initiate civil proceedings, in addition to criminal proceedings provided for in this title, to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(2)(b)(i): recover damages;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(2)(b)(ii): compel performance;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(2)(b)(iii): compel substitution;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(2)(b)(iv): restrain or enjoin;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(2)(b)(v): initiate any other appropriate action; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(2)(b)(vi): seek appropriate remedies in the division's capacity as trustee and custodian.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(3)(a): If a political subdivision of the state adopts an ordinance or regulation concerning hunting, fishing, or trapping that conflicts with this title or rules made pursuant to this title, state law prevails.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(3)(b): A community may close areas to hunting for safety reasons after confirmation by the Wildlife Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(4)(a): As used in this Subsection (4), "claim involving wildlife" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(4)(a)(i): a depredation claim;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(4)(a)(ii): a wildlife damage claim; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(4)(a)(iii): a nuisance complaint involving wildlife.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(4)(b): Subject to Subsection (4)(c), a political subdivision of the state shall respond to and pay for a claim involving wildlife within the boundaries of the political subdivision, if the political subdivision:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(4)(b)(i): owns or purchases an aggregate amount of more than 500 contiguous acres of land in fee simple on which the political subdivision restricts the division's ability to manage wildlife populations; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(4)(b)(ii): enacts an ordinance or takes other action that restricts the division's ability to manage wildlife populations within any portion of the political subdivision's boundary.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(4)(c): A political subdivision of the state may not be required to respond to or pay for a claim involving wildlife under Subsection (4)(b) because the political subdivision has enacted a law, rule, or ordinance or taken an action to prohibit the use of firing a firearm within the boundaries of the political subdivision.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(4)(d): The division may not expend state money for a claim listed in Subsection (4)(b) when a political subdivision limits the division's ability to manage wildlife populations on more than 500 contiguous acres of land.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(5): The division shall comply with Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act, in the division's adjudicative proceedings.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-201(6): The division shall adopt an official seal and file an impression and a description of the official seal with the Division of Archives.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-202 Director of the division -- Qualifications.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-202(1): The director shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-202(1)(a): be the executive and administrative head of the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-202(1)(b): have demonstrated ability in management and administration and experience in the  protection, conservation, restoration, and management of wildlife resources.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-202(2): The director may not hold another public office or be involved in a political party or organization.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-203 Director powers.
------------------------------------------------
The director, under administrative supervision of the executive director, has:Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-203(1): executive authority and control of the division so that policies of the Wildlife Board are carried out in accordance with the laws of this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-203(2): authority over personnel matters;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-203(3): full control of property acquired and held for the purposes specified in this title; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-203(4): authority to declare emergency closed or open seasons in the interest of the wildlife resources of the state.

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
An employee of the division shall receive the compensation the director determines within limits established for state employees by

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-205 Oaths administered by director.
---------------------------------------------------------------
The director may administer oaths for the purposes required in the discharge of the director's duties.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-206 Jurisdiction of division over public or private land and waters.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Wildlife within this state, including wildlife on public or private land or in public or private waters within this state, is within the jurisdiction of the division.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-207 Taking of wildlife by division.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-207(1): Subject to the other provisions of this section, the division may take wildlife of any kind from any place and in any manner for purposes considered by the director to be in the interest of wildlife conservation.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-207(2): The division shall deliver notice to an affected landowner or an agent of an affected landowner, either in writing or orally, before the taking of wildlife on privately owned land under this section. The division may take the wildlife immediately after or at a time reasonably required for the taking after delivering notice.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-207(3): (2) The notice requirements in Subsection

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Notwithstanding any other provision of law, the following may, without obtaining a permit, use fireworks and explosives to rally, drive, or otherwise disperse concentrations of wildlife as may be necessary to protect property or wildlife resources:Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-208(1): an employee of the division designated by the director; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-208(2): a federal game agent charged with the duty of managing wildlife resources.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-303 Regional advisory councils created.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-303(1): There are created five regional advisory councils that consist of 12 to 15 members each from the wildlife region whose boundaries are established for administrative purposes by the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-303(2): The members shall include individuals who represent the following groups and interests:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-303(2)(a): agriculture;

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-303(2)(e): federal land agencies; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-303(2)(f): the public at large.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-303(4): The regional advisory councils shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-303(4)(a): hear broad input, including recommendations, biological data, and information regarding the effects of wildlife;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-303(4)(b): gather information from staff, the public, and government agencies; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-303(4)(c): make recommendations to the Wildlife Board in an advisory capacity.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-303(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-303(5)(a): Except as required by Subsection (5)(b), a member shall serve a four-year term.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-303(5)(b): Notwithstanding the requirements of Subsection (5)(a), the executive director shall, at the time of appointment or reappointment, adjust the length of terms to ensure that the terms of council members are staggered so that approximately half of the council is appointed every two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-303(6): When a vacancy occurs in the membership for any reason, the replacement shall be appointed for the unexpired term.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-303(7): The councils shall determine:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-303(7)(a): the time and place of meetings; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-303(7)(b): a procedural matter not specified in this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-305 Establishment of seasons, locations, limits, and regulations by the Wildlife Board.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-305(1): To provide an adequate and flexible system of protection, propagation, introduction, increase, control, harvest, management, and conservation of protected wildlife in this state and to provide for the use and development of protected wildlife for public recreation and food supply while maintaining a sustainable population of protected wildlife, the Wildlife Board shall determine the circumstances, time, location, means, and the amounts and numbers of protected wildlife that may be taken.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-305(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The Wildlife Board shall, except as otherwise specified in this title:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-305(2)(a): fix seasons and shorten, extend, or close seasons on any species of protected wildlife in any locality, or in the entire state, if the Wildlife Board finds that the action is necessary to effectuate proper wildlife management and control;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-305(2)(b): close or open areas to fishing, trapping, or hunting;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-305(2)(c): establish refuges and preserves;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-305(2)(d): regulate and prescribe the means by which protected wildlife may be taken;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-305(2)(e): regulate the transportation and storage of protected wildlife, or the wildlife parts, within the boundaries of the state and the shipment or transportation out of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-305(2)(f): establish or change bag limits and possession limits;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-305(2)(g): prescribe safety measures and establish other regulations as may be considered necessary in the interest of wildlife conservation and the safety and welfare of hunters, trappers, fishermen, landowners, and the public;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-305(2)(h): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-305(2)(h)(i): prescribe when a license, permit, tag, or certificate of registration is required and procedures for their issuance and use; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-305(2)(h)(ii): establish forms and fees for a license, permit, tag, or certificate of registration; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-305(2)(i): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act make rules, in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-305(3): The Wildlife Board may allow a season on protected wildlife to commence on any day of the week except Sunday.
