Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501 Adoption and text of compact.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(1): (1)(g); (1)(g); (1)(g) The participating states find that:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(1)(a): Wildlife resources are managed in trust by the respective states for the benefit of all residents and visitors.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(1)(b): The protection of the wildlife resources of a state is materially affected by the degree of compliance with state statutes, laws, regulations, ordinances, and administrative rules relating to the management of the resources.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(1)(c): The preservation, protection, management, and restoration of wildlife contributes immeasurably to the aesthetic, recreational, and economic aspects of the natural resources.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(1)(d): Wildlife resources are valuable without regard to political boundaries; therefore, every person should be required to comply with wildlife preservation, protection, management, and restoration laws, ordinances, and administrative rules and regulations of the participating states as a condition precedent to the continuance or issuance of any license to hunt, fish, trap, or possess wildlife.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(1)(e): Violation of wildlife laws interferes with the management of wildlife resources and may endanger the safety of persons and property.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(1)(f): The mobility of many wildlife law violators necessitates the maintenance of channels of communication among the various states.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(1)(g): Usually, a person who is cited for a wildlife violation in a state other than his home state:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(1)(g)(i): is required to post collateral or bond to secure appearance for a trial at a later date; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(1)(g)(ii): is taken directly into custody until collateral or bond is posted; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(1)(g)(iii): is taken directly to court for an immediate appearance.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(1)(h): (1)(g) The purpose of the enforcement practices set forth in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(1)(i): In most instances, a person receiving a wildlife citation in his home state is permitted to accept the citation from the officer at the scene of the violation and immediately continue on his way after agreeing or being instructed to comply with the terms of the citation.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(1)(j): (1)(g) The practices described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(1)(k): (1)(g) The enforcement practices described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(2): 23A-2-503(2) It is the policy of the participating states to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(2)(a): promote compliance with the statutes, laws, ordinances, regulations, and administrative rules relating to the management of wildlife resources in their respective states;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(2)(b): recognize the suspension of wildlife license privileges of a person whose license privileges have been suspended by a participating state and treat the suspension as if it had occurred in their state;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(2)(c): 23A-2-503(2) allow a violator, except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(2)(d): report to the appropriate participating state, as provided in the compact manual, a conviction recorded against a person whose home state was not the issuing state;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(2)(e): allow the home state to recognize and treat convictions recorded against its residents, which convictions occurred in a participating state, as though they had occurred in the home state;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(2)(f): extend cooperation to its fullest extent among the participating states for enforcing compliance with the terms of a wildlife citation issued in one participating state to a resident of another state;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(2)(g): maximize effective use of law enforcement personnel and information; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-501(2)(h): assist court systems in the efficient disposition of wildlife violations.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-502 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this compact:Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-502(1): "Citation" means a summons, complaint, summons and complaint, ticket, penalty assessment, or other official document issued to a person by a wildlife officer or other peace officer for a wildlife violation which contains an order requiring the person to respond.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-502(2): "Collateral" means cash or other security deposited to secure an appearance for trial in connection with the issuance by a wildlife officer or other peace officer of a citation for a wildlife violation.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-502(3): "Compliance" with respect to a citation means the act of answering a citation through an appearance in a court or tribunal, or through the payment of fines, costs, and surcharges.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-502(4): "Conviction" means a conviction, including any court conviction, for an offense related to the preservation, protection, management, or restoration of wildlife which is prohibited by state statute, law, regulation, ordinance, or administrative rule.  This conviction shall also include the forfeiture of any bail, bond, or other security deposited to secure appearance by a person charged with having committed the offense, the payment of a penalty assessment, a plea of nolo contendere and the imposition of a deferred or suspended sentence by the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-502(5): "Court" means a court of law, including magistrate's court and the justice of the peace court.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-502(6): "Home state" means the state of primary residence of a person.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-502(7): "Issuing state" means the participating state which issues a wildlife citation to the violator.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-502(8): "License" means a license, permit, or other public document which conveys to the person to whom it was issued the privilege of pursuing, possessing, or taking any wildlife regulated by statute, law, regulation, ordinance, or administrative rule of a participating state.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-502(9): "Licensing authority" means the department or division within each participating state which is authorized by law to issue or approve licenses or permits to hunt, fish, trap, or possess wildlife.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-502(10): "Participating state" means any state which enacts legislation to become a member of this wildlife compact.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-502(11): "Personal recognizance" means an agreement by a person made at the time of issuance of the wildlife citation that the person will comply with the terms of the citation.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-502(12): "State" means a state, territory, or possession of the United States, the District of Columbia, the Commonwealth of Puerto Rico, the provinces of Canada, and the other countries.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-502(13): "Suspension" means a revocation, denial, or withdrawal of any or all license privileges, including the privilege to apply for, purchase, or exercise the benefits conferred by any license.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-502(14): "Wildlife" means species of animals including, but not limited to, mammals, birds, fish, reptiles, amphibians, mollusks, and crustaceans, which are defined as "wildlife" and are protected or otherwise regulated by statute, law, regulation, ordinance, or administrative rule in a participating state.  Species included in the definition of "wildlife" vary from state to state and determination of whether a species is "wildlife" for the purpose of this compact shall be based on local law.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-502(15): "Wildlife law" means any statute, law, regulation, ordinance, or administrative rule developed and enacted for the management and use of wildlife resources.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-502(16): "Wildlife officer" means an individual authorized by a participating state to issue a citation for a wildlife violation.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-502(17): "Wildlife violation" means a cited violation of a statute, law, regulation, ordinance, or administrative rule developed and enacted for the management and use of wildlife resources.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-503 Procedures for issuing state.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-503(1): (2) When issuing a citation for a wildlife violation, a wildlife officer shall issue a citation to a person whose primary residence is in a participating state in the same manner as though the person were a resident of the issuing state and shall not require the person to post collateral to secure appearance, subject to the exceptions under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-503(2): Personal recognizance is acceptable:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-503(2)(a): if not prohibited by local law or the compact manual; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-503(2)(b): if the violator provides adequate proof of identification to the wildlife officer.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-503(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-503(3)(a): Upon conviction or failure of a person to comply with the terms of a wildlife citation, the appropriate official shall report the conviction or failure to comply to the licensing authority of the participating state in which the wildlife citation was issued.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-503(3)(b): The report shall be made in accordance with procedures specified by the issuing state and shall contain information as specified in the compact manual as minimum requirements for effective processing by the home state.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-503(4): (3)(b) Upon receipt of the report of a conviction or noncompliance pursuant to Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-504 Procedure for home state.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-504(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-504(1)(a): Upon receipt of a report from the licensing authority of the issuing state reporting the failure of a violator to comply with the term of a citation, the licensing authority of the home state shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-504(1)(a)(i): notify the violator;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-504(1)(a)(ii): initiate a suspension action in accordance with the home state's suspension procedures; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-504(1)(a)(iii): suspend the violator's license privileges until satisfactory evidence of compliance with the terms of the wildlife citation has been furnished by the issuing state to the home state licensing authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-504(1)(b): Due process safeguards will be accorded.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-504(2): Upon receipt of a report of conviction from the licensing authority of the issuing state, the licensing authority of the home state shall enter the conviction as though it occurred in the home state for the purposes of the suspension of license privileges.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-504(3): The licensing authority of the home state shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-504(3)(a): maintain a record of actions taken; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-504(3)(b): make reports to issuing states as provided in the compact manual.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-505 Reciprocal recognition of suspension.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-505(1): All participating states shall recognize the suspension of license privileges of a person by the participating state as though the violation resulting in the suspension:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-505(1)(a): had occurred in their state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-505(1)(b): could have been the basis of the suspension of license privileges in their state.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-505(2): Each participating state shall communicate suspension information to other participating states in the form and with the content as contained in the compact manual.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-506 Applicability of other laws.
------------------------------------------------------------
Except as expressly required by provisions of this compact, nothing herein shall be construed to affect the right of any participating state to apply any of its laws relating to license privileges to a person or circumstance or to invalidate or prevent any agreement or other cooperative arrangement between a participating state and a nonparticipating state concerning wildlife law enforcement.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-507 Compact administrator procedures.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-507(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-507(1)(a): A Board of Compact Administrators is established to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-507(1)(a)(i): administer the provisions of this compact; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-507(1)(a)(ii): serve as a governing body for the resolution of all matters relating to the operation of this compact.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-507(1)(b): The board shall be composed of one representative from each of the participating states to be known as the compact administrator.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-507(1)(c): The compact administrator shall be appointed by the head of the licensing authority of each participating state and shall serve and be subject to removal in accordance with the laws of the state he represents.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-507(1)(d): A compact administrator may provide for the discharge of his duties and the performance of his function as a board member by an alternate.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-507(1)(e): An alternate shall not be entitled to serve unless written notification of his identity has been given to the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-507(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-507(2)(a): Each member of the board of compact administrators shall be entitled  to one vote.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-507(2)(b): An action of the board shall not be binding unless taken at a meeting at which a majority of the total number of the board's votes are cast in favor thereof.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-507(2)(c): Action by the board shall be only at a meeting at which a majority of the participating states are represented.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-507(3): The board shall elect annually from its membership a chairman and vice-chairman.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-507(4): The board shall adopt bylaws not inconsistent with the provisions of this compact or the laws of a participating state for the conduct of its business and shall have the power to amend and rescind its bylaws.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-507(5): The board may accept for any of its purposes and functions under this compact any and all donations and grants of money, equipment, supplies, materials, and services, conditional or otherwise, from any state, the United States, or any governmental agency, and may receive, utilize, and dispose of the donations and grants.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-507(6): The board may contract with, or accept services or personnel from, any governmental or intergovernmental agency, individual, firm, or corporation, or any private nonprofit organization or institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-507(7): The board shall formulate all necessary procedures and develop uniform forms and documents for administering the provisions of this compact.  All procedures and forms adopted to board action shall be contained in a compact manual.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-508 Entry into compact and withdrawal.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-508(1): This compact shall become effective at the time it is adopted in substantially similar form by two or more states.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-508(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-508(2)(a): Entry into the compact shall be made by resolution of ratification by the authorized officials of the applying state and submitted to the chairman of the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-508(2)(b): The resolution shall substantially be in the form and content as provided in the compact manual and shall include the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-508(2)(b)(i): a citation of the authority from which the state is empowered to become a party to this compact;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-508(2)(b)(ii): an agreement of compliance with the terms and provisions of this compact; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-508(2)(b)(iii): an agreement that compact entry is with all states participating in the compact and with all additional states legally becoming a party to the compact.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-508(2)(c): The effective date of entry shall be specified by the applying state but shall not be less than 60 days after notice has been given:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-508(2)(c)(i): by the chairman of the board of the compact administrators; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-508(2)(c)(ii): by the secretary of the board to each participating state that the resolution from the applying state has been received.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-508(3): A participating state may withdraw from participation in this compact by official written notice to each participating state, but withdrawal shall not become effective until 90 days after the notice of withdrawal is given.  No withdrawal of any state shall affect the validity of this compact as to the remaining participating states.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-509 Amendments to the compact.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-509(1): This compact may be amended from time to time. Amendments shall be presented in resolution form to the chairman of the Board of Compact Administrators and shall be initiated by one or more participating states.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-509(2): Adoption of an amendment shall require endorsement by all participating states and shall become effective 30 days after the date of the last endorsement.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-509(3): Failure of a participating state to respond to the compact chairman within 120 days after receipt of a proposed amendment shall constitute endorsement thereof.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-510 Construction and severability.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-510(1): This compact shall be liberally construed so as to effectuate the purposes stated herein.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-510(2): The provisions of this compact shall be severable and if a phrase, clause, sentence, or provision of this compact is declared to be contrary to the constitution of a participating state or of the United States, or the applicability thereof to a government, agency, individual, or circumstance is held invalid, the validity of the remainder of this compact shall not be affected thereby.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-510(3): If this compact is held contrary to the constitution of a participating state, the compact shall remain in full force and effect as to the remaining states and in full force and effect as to the participating state affected regarding all severable matters.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-511 Licensing authority -- Administrator -- Expenses.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-511(1): The Division of Wildlife Resources is designated as the licensing authority in this state for the purpose of the compact.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-511(2): The director of the Division of Wildlife Resources shall furnish to the appropriate authorities of the participating states any information or documents reasonably necessary to facilitate the administration of the compact.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-2-511(3): 23A-2-507 The compact administrator provided for in Section


Utah Code Annotated - Title 23A - Chapter 3 - Funds and Accounts

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-101 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
Reserved.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-201 Wildlife Resources Account -- Unexpended fund balances .
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-201(1): There is created a restricted account within the General Fund known as the "Wildlife Resources Account."
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-201(2): 23A-4-306 The following money shall be deposited into the Wildlife Resources Account:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-201(2)(a): revenue from the sale of licenses, permits, tags, and certificates of registration issued under this title or a rule or proclamation of the Wildlife Board, except as otherwise provided by this title;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-201(2)(b): revenue from the sale, lease, rental, or other granting of rights of real or personal property acquired with revenue specified in Subsection (2)(a);
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-201(2)(c): revenue from fines and forfeitures for violations of this title or a rule, proclamation, or order of the Wildlife Board, minus court costs not to exceed the schedule adopted by the Judicial Council;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-201(2)(d): revenue deposited into the fund under Chapter 11, Part 5, Big Game Byproduct;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-201(2)(e): 23A-4-306 money appropriated from the General Fund by the Legislature pursuant to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-201(2)(f): other money received by the division under this title, except as otherwise provided by this title; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-201(2)(g): interest, dividends, or other income earned on account money.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-201(3): Money in the Wildlife Resources Account shall be used for the administration of this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-201(4): At the close of a fiscal year, the unexpended balance in the Wildlife Resources Account shall convert back into the Wildlife Resources Account for the following fiscal year, except for money:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-201(4)(a): legally obligated by contract;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-201(4)(b): designated for capital outlay projects; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-201(4)(c): required for a program extending beyond the close of the fiscal year.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-202 Grants or gifts accepted by division -- Special account.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The division may accept grants or gifts of money, property, water rights or other endowments that benefit the wildlife resources of the state. The division shall place money as received in a special account to be used for specific use as indicated by the grantor.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207 Wildlife Habitat Account.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(1): There is created a restricted account within the General Fund known as the "Wildlife Habitat Account."
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(2): 23A-3-208; (6) The contents of the Wildlife Habitat Account shall consist of:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(2)(a): 23A-3-208 revenue from the sale of licenses, permits, and certificates of registration as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(2)(b): (6) money donated to the division for a purpose specified in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(2)(c): interest and earnings on account money.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(3): 23A-3-208; (4); (6) The division shall use the revenue from the sale of licenses, permits, and certificates of registration that is deposited to the account pursuant to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(4)(a): The division shall allocate in a fiscal year up to $70,000 or 10% of the annual deposits to the Wildlife Habitat Account, whichever amount is greater, for the development, restoration, and preservation of wetlands that are beneficial to waterfowl.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(4)(b): Up to 20% of the money allocated to waterfowl projects may be appropriated by the Legislature for use by a nonprofit conservation organization for wetland development projects within the state that benefit waterfowl.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(5)(a): The division shall allocate in a fiscal year up to $230,000 or 10% of the annual deposits to the Wildlife Habitat Account, whichever amount is greater, to upland game projects as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(5)(a)(i): the control of predators;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(5)(a)(ii): the development, improvement, restoration, or maintenance of critical habitat through the establishment of landowner incentives, cooperative programs, or other means;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(5)(a)(iii): the acquisition or preservation of critical habitat;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(5)(a)(iv): landowner habitat education and assistance programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(5)(a)(v): public access to private lands; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(5)(a)(vi): upland game transplant and reintroduction programs.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(5)(b): Money allocated to upland game may not be used for the acquisition, development, improvement, restoration, or maintenance of habitat within commercial hunting areas.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(5)(c): No more than 5% of the money allocated to upland game may be used for landowner habitat education programs.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(5)(d): The division shall use money allocated to upland game for programs and activities relating to upland game species based generally upon the proportion of average annual hunter participation for each species.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(5)(e): Projects for which free public access is assured shall receive first priority for funding from money allocated to upland game.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(5)(f): Projects for which public access is assured shall receive second priority for funding from money allocated to upland game.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(6): The division shall use remaining money in the Wildlife Habitat Account for the following purposes:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(6)(a): the enhancement, acquisition, preservation, protection, and management of aquatic and terrestrial wildlife habitat; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(6)(b): to improve access for fishing and hunting.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(7): The division shall seek the advice and recommendations of the Habitat Council, created by the division, regarding the expenditure of account money.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(8): Donations of money deposited into the Wildlife Habitat Account and interest earned on that money shall be expended:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(8)(a): as directed by the donor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-207(8)(b): without being appropriated by the Legislature.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-208 Portion of revenue from license, permit, and certificate of registration fees deposited into Wildlife Habitat Account.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-209 Predator Control Restricted Account.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-209(1): There is created a restricted account within the General Fund known as the "Predator Control Restricted Account."
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-209(2): 23A-4-703 The Predator Control Restricted Account includes:

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-209(2)(b): other amounts deposited in the Predator Control Restricted Account from donations or appropriations.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-209(3): The division shall use money from the Predator Control Restricted Account to fund a predator control program to control populations of predatory animals that endanger the health of nonpredatory wildlife populations in the state, consistent with the policies of the Wildlife Board.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-210 State Fish Hatchery Maintenance Account.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-210(1): There is created a restricted account within the General Fund known as the "State Fish Hatchery Maintenance Account."
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-210(2): The following money shall be deposited into the State Fish Hatchery Maintenance Account:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-210(2)(a): $4 of a fishing license fee or combination license fee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-210(2)(b): interest and earnings on account money.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-210(3): The division, after appropriation by the Legislature, shall use money in the State Fish Hatchery Maintenance Account for major repairs or replacement of facilities and equipment at fish hatcheries owned and operated by the division for the production and distribution of fish to enhance sport fishing opportunities in the state.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-214 Species Protection Account.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-214(1): There is created within the General Fund a restricted account known as the Species Protection Account.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-214(2): The account shall consist of:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-214(2)(a): revenue generated by the brine shrimp tax provided for in Title 59, Chapter 23, Brine Shrimp Royalty Act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-214(2)(b): interest earned on money in the account.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-214(3): Money in the account may be appropriated by the Legislature to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-214(3)(a): develop and implement species status assessments and species protection measures;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-214(3)(b): obtain biological opinions of proposed species protection measures;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-214(3)(c): conduct studies, investigations, and research into the effects of proposed species protection measures;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-214(3)(d): verify species protection proposals that are not based on valid biological data;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-214(3)(e): implement Great Salt Lake wetlands mitigation projects in connection with the western transportation corridor;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-214(3)(f): pay for the state's voluntary contributions to the Utah Reclamation Mitigation and Conservation Account under the Central Utah Project Completion Act, Pub. L. No. 102-575, Titles II-VI, 106 Stat. 4605-4655; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-214(3)(g): pay for expenses of the State Tax Commission under Title 59, Chapter 23, Brine Shrimp Royalty Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-214(4): The purposes specified in Subsections (3)(a) through (3)(d) may be accomplished by the state or, in an appropriation act, the Legislature may authorize the department to award grants to political subdivisions of the state to accomplish those purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-214(5): Money in the account may not be used to develop or implement a habitat conservation plan required under federal law unless the federal government pays for at least 1/3 of the habitat conservation plan costs.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-306 Uses of legacy fund.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-306(1): Each year, when the board creates a budget, the board shall allocate:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-306(1)(a): 40% of the budget:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-306(1)(a)(i): for staff and expenses to administer the legacy fund under this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-306(1)(a)(ii): to conduct research, monitoring, and management actions that benefit non-game species; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-306(1)(a)(iii): to otherwise reduce the likelihood of future species listings under the Endangered Species Act, 16 U.S.C. Sec. 1531 et seq.; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-306(1)(b): 60% of the budget to fund the following projects that provide the following landscape level conservation benefits:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-306(1)(b)(i): preserving open spaces, wildlife habitat, and critical agricultural lands;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-306(1)(b)(ii): providing perpetual access for hunting, fishing, or trapping;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-306(1)(b)(iii): addressing and mitigating impacts detrimental to wildlife habitat, the environment, and the multiple use of renewable natural resources attributable to residential, mineral, and industrial development; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-306(1)(b)(iv): preserving a viable agricultural industry.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-306(2): (1)(b); (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-306(2)(a): (1)(b) The board shall make recommendations to the division regarding expenditures from the legacy fund for the purposes described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-306(2)(b): (1) The division shall consider the board's recommendations in approving an expenditure from the legacy fund under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-306(3): (1)(b); 23A-6-202 In performing the actions described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-306(4): This section does not give the division the power of eminent domain.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-306(5): The division may not use assets from the legacy fund for litigation.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-3-306(6): Money in the legacy fund may not be used to develop or implement a habitat conservation plan required under federal law unless the federal government pays for at least one-third of the habitat conservation plan costs.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-203 Tag as supplement to licenses and permits.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
The division may issue, as a supplement to the appropriate license or permit, a tag for protected wildlife, as determined by the Wildlife Board.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-204 Alien's and nonresident peace officer's ability to obtain licenses and certificates.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-204(1): An alien resident of Utah may purchase a hunting, fishing, trapping, seining, and fur dealer license or certificate of registration upon the same terms as a resident citizen.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-204(2): A nonresident alien may purchase a hunting, fishing, trapping, seining, or fur dealer license or certificate of registration upon the same terms as nonresident citizens.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-204(3)(b): required to live outside the state as a condition of the person's employment.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-208 Duplicate license, permit, tag, or certificate of registration.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-208(1): If an unexpired license, permit, tag, or certificate of registration issued under this title is destroyed, lost, or stolen, the division, a person designated by the director, or the division's authorized license agents may issue a duplicate license, permit, tag, or certificate of registration in accordance with the rules set and fees determined by the Wildlife Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-208(2): Upon issuance of a duplicate license, permit, tag, or certificate of registration, the original license, permit, tag, or certificate of registration is invalid.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-301 Refunds for armed forces or public health or safety organization members.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-301(1): (2) A member of the United States Armed Forces or public health or public safety organization who is mobilized or deployed on order in the interest of national defense or emergency and is precluded from using a purchased license, certificate, tag, or permit, may, as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-301(1)(a): receive a refund from the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-301(1)(b): if the person has drawn a permit, have the opportunities to draw that permit in a future draw reinstated.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-301(2): To qualify, the person or a legal representative shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-301(2)(a): notify the division within a reasonable amount of time that the person is applying for a refund;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-301(2)(b): surrender the license, certificate, tag, or permit to the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-301(2)(c): furnish satisfactory proof to the division that the person:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-301(2)(c)(i): is a member of:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-301(2)(c)(i)(A): the United States Armed Forces;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-301(2)(c)(i)(B): a public health organization; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-301(2)(c)(i)(C): a public safety organization; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-301(2)(c)(ii): was precluded from using the license, certificate, tag, or permit as a result of being called to active duty.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304 Persons participating in youth organization or school activity may fish without license.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(1)(a): "School" means an elementary school or a secondary school that:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(1)(a)(i): is a public or private school located in the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(1)(a)(ii): provides student instruction for one or more years of kindergarten through grade 9.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(1)(b): "Youth organization" means a local Utah chapter of:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(1)(b)(i): the Boy Scouts of America;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(1)(b)(ii): the Girls Scouts of the USA; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(1)(b)(iii): an organization that:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(1)(b)(iii)(A): is exempt from taxation under Section 501(c)(3), Internal Revenue Code; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(1)(b)(iii)(B): promotes character building through outdoor activities.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(2): The division shall permit a person to fish without a license during a youth organization or school activity if:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(2)(a): the person is:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(2)(a)(i): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(2)(a)(i)(A): a member of the youth organization; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(2)(a)(i)(B): a student enrolled in the school; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(2)(a)(ii): younger than 16 years old;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(2)(b): the fishing is in compliance with the fishing statutes and rules;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(2)(c): the activity is part of a recreational or instructional program of the youth organization or school; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(2)(d): an adult leader of the activity obtains from the youth organization or school:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(2)(d)(i): a valid tour permit; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(2)(d)(ii): documentation that specifies:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(2)(d)(ii)(A): the date and place of the fishing activity;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(2)(d)(ii)(B): the name of the adult leader that will supervise the fishing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(2)(d)(ii)(C): that the activity is officially sanctioned or authorized by the youth organization or school.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(3): (3)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(3)(a): The adult leader shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(3)(a)(i): possess a valid Utah fishing or combination license; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(3)(a)(ii): instruct the activity participants on fishing statutes and rules.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-304(3)(b): (3)(a) The division shall provide educational materials on the division's website to assist the adult leader in complying with Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-305 Persons with a physical or intellectual disability, terminally ill persons, and children in the custody of the state may fish for free.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-305(1): A resident who is blind, has paraplegia, or has another permanent disability so as to be permanently confined to a wheelchair or the use of crutches, or who has lost either or both lower extremities, may receive a free license to fish upon furnishing satisfactory proof of this fact to the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-305(2): 23A-4-303 A resident who has an intellectual disability and is not eligible under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-305(3): A resident who is terminally ill, and has less than five years to live, may receive a free license to fish:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-305(3)(a): upon furnishing verification from a physician or physician assistant; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-305(3)(b): if the resident qualifies for assistance under a low income public assistance program administered by a state agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-305(4): A child placed in the custody of the state by a court order may receive a free fishing license upon furnishing verification of custody to the division.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-401 Resident fishing and hunting license -- Use of fee.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-401(1): A resident, after paying the fee established by the Wildlife Board, may obtain, as provided by the Wildlife Board's rules, a combination license to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-401(1)(a): fish;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-401(1)(b): hunt for small game;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-401(1)(c): hunt or trap cougar during a period beginning on January 1 and ending on December 31; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-401(1)(d): apply for or obtain a big game,, bear, or turkey hunting permit.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-401(2): Up to $1 of the combination license fee may be used for the hunter education program for any of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-401(2)(a): instructor and student training;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-401(2)(b): assisting local organizations with development;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-401(2)(c): maintenance of existing facilities; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-401(2)(d): operation and maintenance of the hunter education program.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-401(3)(a): Up to 50 cents of the combination license fee may be used for the upland game program to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-401(3)(a)(i): acquire pen-raised birds; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-401(3)(a)(ii): capture and transplant upland game species.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-501 Wildlife license agents.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-501(1): The director may designate wildlife license agents to sell licenses, permits, and tags.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-501(2): 23A-4-503(2) A wildlife license agent may:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-501(2)(a): 23A-4-503(2) sell a license, permit, or tag to an eligible applicant, except for a license, permit, or tag specified in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-501(2)(b): collect a fee for a license, permit, or tag sold.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-501(3): A wildlife license agent shall receive:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-501(3)(a): for a wildlife license, permit, or tag having a fee equal to $10 or less but greater than $1, 50 cents for a wildlife license, permit, or tag sold; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-501(3)(b): for a wildlife license, permit, or tag having a fee greater than $10, 5% of the fee.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-501(4): The division may require a wildlife license agent to obtain a bond in a reasonable amount.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-501(5): (3); (3)
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-501(5)(a): (3) As directed by the division, a wildlife license agent shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-501(5)(a)(i): report the wildlife license agent's sales to the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-501(5)(a)(ii): (3) submit to the division the fees obtained from the sale of licenses, permits, and tags less the remuneration provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-501(5)(b): If a wildlife license agent fails to pay the amount due, the division may assess a penalty of 20% of the amount due. A delinquent payment shall bear interest at the rate of 1% per month.  If the amount due is not paid because of bad faith or fraud, the division shall assess a penalty of 100% of the total amount due together with interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-501(5)(c): (3) Fees, except the remuneration provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-501(5)(c)(i): be kept separate from the private money of the wildlife license agents; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-501(5)(c)(ii): belong to the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-501(6): 23A-4-1001; 23A-4-1005 A wildlife license agent may not intentionally:

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-601 Fishing license.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-601(1): A person 12 years old or older shall purchase a fishing license before engaging in a regulated fishing activity.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-601(2): Upon paying the fee prescribed by the Wildlife Board, a person may obtain a license to fish and engage in a regulated fishing activity in accordance with the rules, proclamations, and orders of the Wildlife Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-601(3): A person under 12 years old may fish without a license in accordance with the rules, proclamations, and orders of the Wildlife Board.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-602 Seining registration.
-----------------------------------------------------
A person, upon application to the Wildlife Board, may be registered to seine.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-702 Air rifle hunting.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-702(1): As used in this section, "pre-charged pneumatic air rifle" means a rifle that fires a single projectile with compressed air released from a chamber:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-702(1)(a): built into the rifle; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-702(1)(b): pressurized at a minimum of 2,000 pounds per square inch from an external high compression device or source, such as a hand pump, compressor, or scuba tank.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-702(2): An individual may use a pre-charged pneumatic air rifle to hunt:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-702(2)(a): a species of protected wildlife designated by the Wildlife Board;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-702(2)(b): a cottontail rabbit;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-702(2)(c): a snowshoe hare; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-702(2)(d): a turkey, with a fall turkey permit.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-702(3): The division shall review available funding to pay the costs of regulating hunting with pre-charged pneumatic air rifles, including eligibility for federal excise taxes, and report the division's findings to the Natural Resources, Agriculture, and Environment Interim Committee by no later than the November 2024 interim committee meeting.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-703(1): (4) A person who is at least 12 years old may apply for or obtain a permit to hunt big game as provided by a rule or proclamation of the Wildlife Board upon:

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-703(1)(b): (4) paying the fee established by Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-703(2)(b): A person may not use a permit to hunt big game before the person's 12th birthday.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-703(3): 23A-4-401 The division shall use one dollar of a big game permit fee collected from a resident for the hunter education program as provided in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-704 Bear hunting permit.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-704(1): A person 12 years old or older may apply for or obtain a permit to take bear as provided by a rule or proclamation of the Wildlife Board upon:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-704(1)(a): paying the bear hunting permit fee established by the Wildlife Board; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-704(1)(b): possessing a valid hunting or combination license.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-704(2): A person 11 years old may apply for or obtain a bear hunting permit consistent with the requirements of Subsection (1) if that person's 12th birthday falls within the calendar year in which the permit is issued.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-704(3): The division shall use one dollar of a bear permit fee collected from a resident for the hunter education program.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-705 Turkey hunting permit -- Use of fee.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-705(1): A person may apply for or obtain a permit to take turkey as provided by a rule or proclamation of the Wildlife Board upon:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-705(1)(a): paying the turkey permit fee established by the Wildlife Board; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-705(1)(b): possessing a valid hunting or combination license.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-705(2): The division shall use one dollar of a turkey permit fee collected from a resident for the hunter education program.

-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-706(1): A resident may obtain a hunting license after paying the fee established by the Wildlife Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-706(2): A hunting license authorizes the licensee to, according to this title and the Wildlife Board's rules and proclamations:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-706(2)(a): take small game;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-706(2)(b): hunt or trap cougar during a period beginning on January 1 and ending on December 31; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-706(2)(c): apply for or obtain a big game, bear, or turkey hunting permit.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-706(3): Up to $1 of the hunting license fee may be used for the hunter education program.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-706(4)(a)(ii): capture and transplant upland game species.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-707 Nonresident hunting license -- Use of fee.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-707(1): A nonresident may obtain a hunting license after paying the fee established by the Wildlife Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-707(2): A hunting license authorizes the licensee to, according to this title and the Wildlife Board's rules and proclamations:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-707(2)(a): take small game;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-707(2)(b): hunt or trap cougar during a period beginning on January 1 and ending on December 31; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-707(2)(c): apply for or obtain a big game, bear, or turkey hunting permit.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-707(3): (3)(a); 23A-3-207; 23A-3-208
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-707(3)(a): Up to 50 cents of the hunting license fee may be used for the upland game program to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-707(3)(a)(i): acquire pen-raised birds; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-707(3)(a)(ii): capture and transplant upland game species.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-707(3)(b): (3)(a); 23A-3-207; 23A-3-208 The hunting license fee revenue designated for the upland game program by Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-708 Children accompanied by adults while hunting with weapon.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-708(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-708(1)(a): "Accompanied" means at a distance within which visual and verbal communication is maintained for the purposes of advising and assisting.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-708(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-708(1)(b)(i): "Electronic device" means a mechanism powered by electricity that allows communication between two or more people.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-708(1)(b)(ii): "Electronic device" includes a mobile telephone or two-way radio.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-708(1)(c): "Verbal communication" means the conveyance of information through speech that does not involve an electronic device.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-708(2): A person younger than 14 years old who is hunting with a weapon shall be accompanied by:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-708(2)(a): the person's parent or legal guardian; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-708(2)(b): a responsible person who is at least 21 years old and who is approved by the person's parent or guardian.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-708(3): A person younger than 16 years old who is hunting big game with a weapon shall be accompanied by:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-708(3)(a): the person's parent or legal guardian; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-708(3)(b): a responsible person who is at least 21 years old and who is approved by the person's parent or guardian.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-708(4): A person who is at least 14 years old but younger than 16 years old shall be accompanied by a person who is at least 21 years old while hunting wildlife, other than big game, with a weapon.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-709 Tagging requirements.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-709(1): The Wildlife Board may make rules that require the carcass of certain species of protected wildlife to be tagged.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-709(2): Except as provided by the Wildlife Board by rules made in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, a hunter who lawfully killed the animal shall tag the carcass of a species of protected wildlife required to be tagged before the carcass is moved from or the hunter leaves the site of kill.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-709(3): To tag a carcass, a person shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-709(3)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-709(3)(a)(i): completely detach the tag from the license or permit;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-709(3)(a)(ii): completely remove the appropriate notches to correspond with:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-709(3)(a)(ii)(A): the date the animal was taken; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-709(3)(a)(ii)(B): the sex of the animal; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-709(3)(a)(iii): attach the tag to the carcass so that the tag remains securely fastened and visible; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-709(3)(b): complete an electronic tagging certification according to standards approved by the Wildlife Board by rule made in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-709(4): A person may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-709(4)(a): remove more than one notch indicating date or sex; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-709(4)(b): tag more than one carcass using the same tag.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-710 Hunting Mentor Program.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-710(1): As used in this section, "immediate family member" means a spouse, child, parent, sibling, grandparent, grandchild, parent-in-law, child-in-law, sibling-in-law, or stepchild.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-710(2): A resident or nonresident minor under 18 years old may use the hunting permit of another person if:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-710(2)(a): the permit holder:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-710(2)(a)(i): receives no form of compensation or remuneration for allowing the minor to use the permit;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-710(2)(a)(ii): obtains the division's prior written approval to allow the minor to use the permit; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-710(2)(a)(iii): accompanies the minor, for the purposes of advising and assisting during the hunt, at a distance where the permit holder can communicate with the minor, in person, by voice or visual signals; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-710(2)(b): the minor is otherwise legally eligible to hunt.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-710(3): If the permit holder dies before the hunt authorized by the permit described in this section, the minor may use the permit if the minor is:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-710(3)(a): an immediate family member of the permit holder; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-710(3)(b): accompanied by an adult immediate family member while using the permit.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-710(4): This section does not convey any property interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-710(5): The Wildlife Board shall issue a permit in accordance with this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-901 Furbearer license -- Resident or nonresident.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
A resident or nonresident may receive a license to take furbearers upon payment of the fee prescribed by the Wildlife Board.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-902 Resident fur dealer registration.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
A resident may be registered as a fur dealer upon application to the Wildlife Board.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-903 Nonresident fur dealer registration.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
A nonresident may be registered as a fur dealer upon application to the Wildlife Board.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-904 Registration of fur dealer's agent.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
A person who is employed by a fur dealer as a fur buyer in the field may be registered as a fur dealer's agent upon application to the Wildlife Board.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-905 Fur dealer and fur dealer's agent -- Certificates of registration required -- Receipts required.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-905(1): (1)(b)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-905(1)(a): A person engaging in, carrying on, or conducting, wholly or in part, the business of buying, selling, trading, or dealing, within the state, in the skins or pelts of furbearing mammals is considered a fur dealer within the meaning of this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-905(1)(b): (1)(b)(i) A fur dealer shall secure a fur dealer certificate of registration from the division, except a certificate of registration is not required for:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-905(1)(b)(i): a licensed trapper or fur farmer selling skins or pelts that the licensed trapper or fur farmer has lawfully taken or raised; or

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-905(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-905(2)(a): A person who is employed by a resident or nonresident fur dealer as a fur buyer, in the field, is considered a fur dealer's agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-905(2)(b): The fur dealer employing an agent shall apply for a fur dealer's agent certificate of registration, and an agent certificate of registration may not be issued until the necessary fur dealer certificate of registration has been first secured by the employer of the agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-905(3): The vendor shall issue a receipt to the vendee whenever the skins or pelts of furbearing mammals change ownership by virtue of sale, exchange, barter, or gift. Both the vendor and vendee shall produce the receipt or evidence of legal transaction upon request by the division or other person authorized to enforce this title.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1006(1)(h): trapper health and safety; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1006(1)(i): ethics relating to the avoidance of conflicts with other public land users and private landowners.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1006(2)(b): Upon the successful completion of the course, the division shall issue to the participant in the furharvester education course a certificate of completion in furharvester education.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1107 Violation of suspension -- Criminal penalty.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1107(1): A person may not apply for, purchase, possess, or attempt to exercise the benefits conferred by a permit, license, or certificate of registration specified in an order of suspension while that order is in effect.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1107(2): (1) A person who violates Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1107(3): A license possessed or obtained in violation of the order is invalid.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1108 Court-ordered action against a license.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
The division shall promptly withhold, suspend, restrict, or reinstate the use of a license issued under this chapter if so ordered by a court.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1109 Warrant outstanding or failure to comply with citation -- Person not entitled to license, permit, tag, or certificate.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1109(1): Chapter 2, Part 5, Wildlife Violator Compact A person may not purchase a license, permit, tag, or certificate of registration if:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1109(1)(a): there is an outstanding Utah warrant against the person for failure to appear in answer to a summons for a violation of:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1109(1)(a)(i): this title; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1109(1)(a)(ii): a rule, proclamation, or order of the Wildlife Board; or

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1109(2)(a): the warrant is no longer outstanding; or
