Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1110 Invalid and forfeited permit or tag.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1110(1): With each issued permit or tag, a person may take only one of a species of protected wildlife during a license year, regardless of how many licenses or permits the person obtains, except as otherwise provided by this title or a proclamation of the Wildlife Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1110(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1110(2)(a): If a person kills an animal in violation of this title, while attempting to exercise the benefits of an issued permit or tag, the permit or tag is invalid and the person shall forfeit the permit or tag to the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1110(2)(b): This Subsection (2) does not apply if:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1110(2)(b)(i): a citation is issued for a rule violation described in Subsection (2)(a); or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1110(2)(b)(ii): a warning citation for a violation described in Subsection (2)(a) is issued.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1110(3): The division may grant a season extension to a valid, unfilled permit opportunity that was invalidated and forfeited under Subsection (2) if:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1110(3)(a): the criminal charges associated with the permit forfeiture are dismissed, with prejudice, by action of the prosecutor or court, or acquittal of the charges at trial;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1110(3)(b): the person issued the permit that is forfeited requests the division in writing within 60 days of a final action dismissing or acquitting that person of the criminal charges that led to the permit forfeiture;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1110(3)(c): the season extension is granted for the same species and sex, hunt unit, and season dates associated with the forfeited permit, as established by the Wildlife Board in the hunt year of the extension; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-4-1110(3)(d): the extension occurs in the first season immediately following dismissal of or acquittal on the criminal charges described in Subsection (3)(a).


Utah Code Annotated - Title 23A - Chapter 5 - Enforcement and Violations
************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-101 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
Reserved.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201 Enforcement authority of conservation officers -- Seizure and disposition of property.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(1): A conservation officer shall enforce the provisions of this title in accordance with the same procedures and requirements for a law enforcement officer of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(2)(a): Except as provided in Subsection (2)(b), a conservation officer may seize property or contraband in accordance with Title 77, Chapter 11a, Seizure of Property and Contraband, and Title 77, Chapter 11b, Forfeiture of Seized Property.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(2)(b): A conservation officer shall seize protected wildlife illegally taken or held.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(3)(a): If a conservation officer seizes wildlife as part of an investigation or prosecution of an offense and the wildlife may reasonably be used to incriminate or exculpate a person for the offense, the division is not required to retain the wildlife under Title 77, Chapter 11c, Retention of Evidence.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(3)(b): If the division does not retain wildlife under Subsection (3)(a), the division is required to preserve sufficient evidence from the wildlife for use as evidence in the prosecution of a person for the offense.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(4)(a): If a conservation officer seizes wildlife and the wildlife or parts of the wildlife are perishable, the division may donate the wildlife or parts of the wildlife to be used for charitable purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(4)(b): If wildlife or parts of the wildlife are perishable and are not fit to be donated for charitable purposes under Subsection (4)(a), the division may dispose of the wildlife or parts of the wildlife in a reasonable manner.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(5)(a): If a defendant is convicted of the offense for which protected wildlife is seized and the division is permitted by law to sell or dispose of the protected wildlife, the division may sell or dispose of the protected wildlife or part of the wildlife.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(5)(b): The division may not sell migratory wildfowl but the division shall donate the migratory wildfowl to be used for charitable purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(5)(c): The division shall deposit the proceeds from the sale of protected wildlife into the Wildlife Resources Account.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(6): 23A-5-312 If the division disposes of wildlife and the defendant is acquitted of the offense for which the wildlife is seized or the entire case for the offense is dismissed, the court may order the division to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(6)(a): provide the owner of the disposed wildlife with wildlife that is reasonably equivalent in value to the disposed wildlife within 180 days after the day on which the court enters the order; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(6)(b): 23A-5-312 if the division is unable to obtain wildlife that is reasonably equivalent in value to the disposed wildlife, pay the owner of the disposed wildlife for the non-trophy value of the disposed wildlife in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7): 77-11a-201
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7)(a): 77-11a-201 If a conservation officer seizes a vehicle under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7)(b): The division shall release a seized vehicle to the owner no later than 30 days after the day on which the vehicle is seized, unless the vehicle was used for the unlawful taking or possessing of wildlife by a person charged with a felony under this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7)(c): The owner of a seized vehicle is liable for the payment of any impound fee if:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7)(c)(i): the owner used the vehicle for the unlawful taking or possessing of wildlife; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7)(c)(ii): the owner is convicted of an offense under this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7)(d): The owner of a seized vehicle is not liable for the payment of any impound fee or, if the fees have been paid, is entitled to reimbursement of the fees paid, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7)(d)(i): no charges are filed or all charges are dropped that involve the use of the vehicle for the unlawful taking or possessing of wildlife;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7)(d)(ii): the person charged with using the vehicle for the unlawful taking or possessing of wildlife is found by a court to be not guilty; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7)(d)(iii): the owner did not consent to a use of the vehicle that violates this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201 Enforcement authority of natural resources officers -- Seizure and disposition of property.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(1): A natural resources officer shall enforce the provisions of this title in accordance with the same procedures and requirements for a law enforcement officer of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(2)(a): Except as provided in Subsection (2)(b), a natural resources officer may seize property or contraband in accordance with Title 77, Chapter 11a, Seizure of Property and Contraband, and Title 77, Chapter 11b, Forfeiture of Seized Property.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(2)(b): A natural resources officer shall seize protected wildlife illegally taken or held.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(3)(a): If a natural resources officer seizes wildlife as part of an investigation or prosecution of an offense and the wildlife may reasonably be used to incriminate or exculpate a person for the offense, the Division of Law Enforcement is not required to retain the wildlife under Title 77, Chapter 11c, Retention of Evidence.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(3)(b): If the Division of Law Enforcement does not retain wildlife under Subsection (3)(a), the Division of Law Enforcement is required to preserve sufficient evidence from the wildlife for use as evidence in the prosecution of a person for the offense.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(4)(a): If a natural resources officer seizes wildlife and the wildlife or parts of the wildlife are perishable, the Division of Law Enforcement may donate the wildlife or parts of the wildlife to be used for charitable purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(4)(b): If wildlife or parts of the wildlife are perishable and are not fit to be donated for charitable purposes under Subsection (4)(a), the Division of Law Enforcement may dispose of the wildlife or parts of the wildlife in a reasonable manner.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(5)(a): If a defendant is convicted of the offense for which protected wildlife is seized and the Division of Law Enforcement is permitted by law to sell or dispose of the protected wildlife, the Division of Law Enforcement may sell or dispose of the protected wildlife or part of the wildlife.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(5)(b): The Division of Law Enforcement may not sell migratory wildfowl but the Division of Law Enforcement shall donate the migratory wildfowl to be used for charitable purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(5)(c): The Division of Law Enforcement shall deposit the proceeds from the sale of protected wildlife into the Wildlife Resources Account.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(6): 23A-5-312 If the Division of Law Enforcement disposes of wildlife and the defendant is acquitted of the offense for which the wildlife is seized or the entire case for the offense is dismissed, the court may order the Division of Law Enforcement to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(6)(a): provide the owner of the disposed wildlife with wildlife that is reasonably equivalent in value to the disposed wildlife within 180 days after the day on which the court enters the order; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(6)(b): 23A-5-312 if the Division of Law Enforcement is unable to obtain wildlife that is reasonably equivalent in value to the disposed wildlife, pay the owner of the disposed wildlife for the non-trophy value of the disposed wildlife in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7): 77-11a-201
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7)(a): 77-11a-201 If a natural resources officer seizes a vehicle under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7)(b): The Division of Law Enforcement shall release a seized vehicle to the owner no later than 30 days after the day on which the vehicle is seized, unless the vehicle was used for the unlawful taking or possessing of wildlife by a person charged with a felony under this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7)(c): The owner of a seized vehicle is liable for the payment of any impound fee if:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7)(c)(i): the owner used the vehicle for the unlawful taking or possessing of wildlife; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7)(c)(ii): the owner is convicted of an offense under this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7)(d): The owner of a seized vehicle is not liable for the payment of any impound fee or, if the fees have been paid, is entitled to reimbursement of the fees paid, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7)(d)(i): no charges are filed or all charges are dropped that involve the use of the vehicle for the unlawful taking or possessing of wildlife;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7)(d)(ii): the person charged with using the vehicle for the unlawful taking or possessing of wildlife is found by a court to be not guilty; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-201(7)(d)(iii): the owner did not consent to a use of the vehicle that violates this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-202 Powers of law enforcement section.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-202(1): The chief and assistant chief of the law enforcement section or conservation officer of the law enforcement section within the division are vested with the powers of law enforcement officers throughout the counties of the state with exception of the power to serve civil process and:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-202(1)(a): may serve criminal process, arrest, and prosecute a violator of a law of this state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-202(1)(b): has the same right as other law enforcement officers to require aid in executing the duties.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-202(2): The powers and duties conferred by this section upon employees of the law enforcement section of the division shall be supplementary to and in no way a limitation on the powers and duties of other law enforcement officers in the state.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-203 Special deputies -- Appointment -- Duties.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
The director may appoint a person, on a temporary basis, as a special deputy. A special deputy may enforce this title and rules made under this title.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-204 Butcher, locker, or storage plant to require proper tag or donation slip -- Taxidermist.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-204(1): A butcher or owner or employee of a locker plant or storage plant may not receive for processing or storage the carcass of protected wildlife that by law or regulation is required to be tagged, unless there is a transaction record for the carcass which is that the carcass is:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-204(1)(a): properly tagged; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-204(1)(b): accompanied with a valid donation slip.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-204(2): A taxidermist shall retain the transaction records for wildlife received, to include:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-204(2)(a): the date and time the wildlife is received; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-204(2)(b): the license or permit number associated with the wildlife.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-204(3): A person required to retain a transaction record under this section shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-204(3)(a): produce the transaction record on the demand of a peace officer; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-204(3)(b): keep the transaction record for three years from the day on which the person receives or creates the transaction record.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-205 Enforcement -- Procedure.
---------------------------------------------------------
In enforcing the misdemeanor or felony provisions of this title, a peace officer shall follow

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206 Search warrants.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(1): A search warrant may be issued by a magistrate to search for property that may constitute evidence of a violation of this title, rules, or proclamations of the Wildlife Board upon an affidavit of a person.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(2): The search warrant shall be directed to a conservation officer or a peace officer, directing the officer to search for evidence and to bring the evidence before the magistrate.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(3): A search warrant may not be issued except upon probable cause supported by oath or affirmation, particularly describing the place, person, or thing to be searched for and the person or thing to be seized.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(4): The warrant shall be served in the daytime, unless there is reason to believe that the service of the search warrant is required immediately because a person may:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(4)(a): flee the jurisdiction to avoid prosecution or discovery of a violation noted above;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(4)(b): destroy or conceal evidence of the commission of a violation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(4)(c): injure another person or damage property.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(5): (4) Notwithstanding Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(5)(a): there is reason to believe that a violation may occur at night; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(5)(b): the evidence of the violation may not be available to the officers serving the warrant during the day.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206 Search warrants.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(1): A search warrant may be issued by a magistrate to search for property that may constitute evidence of a violation of this title, rules, or proclamations of the Wildlife Board upon an affidavit of a person.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(2): The search warrant shall be directed to a natural resources officer or a peace officer, directing the officer to search for evidence and to bring the evidence before the magistrate.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(3): A search warrant may not be issued except upon probable cause supported by oath or affirmation, particularly describing the place, person, or thing to be searched for and the person or thing to be seized.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(4): The warrant shall be served in the daytime, unless there is reason to believe that the service of the search warrant is required immediately because a person may:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(4)(a): flee the jurisdiction to avoid prosecution or discovery of a violation noted above;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(4)(b): destroy or conceal evidence of the commission of a violation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(4)(c): injure another person or damage property.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(5): Notwithstanding Subsection (4), a search warrant may be served at night if:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(5)(a): there is reason to believe that a violation may occur at night; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-206(5)(b): the evidence of the violation may not be available to the officers serving the warrant during the day.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-207 Exhibition of license, permit, tag, or device required -- Criminal penalty.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-207(1): A person while engaged in an activity regulated under this title, shall exhibit the following at the request of conservation officer or other peace officer:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-207(1)(a): the required license, permit, or tag;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-207(1)(b): device or apparatus in that person's possession used for an activity regulated under this title; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-207(1)(c): wildlife in that person's possession.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-207(2): A conservation officer who has a reasonable belief that a person is engaged in an activity regulated under this title may stop and temporarily detain that person to demand and inspect:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-207(2)(a): the required license, permit, or tag;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-207(2)(b): a device or apparatus in that person's possession used for an activity regulated under this title; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-207(2)(c): wildlife in that person's possession.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-207(3): 23A-5-301 A person is subject to the penalties of Section


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-207 Exhibition of license, permit, tag, or device required -- Criminal penalty.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-307(4)(b): A trail camera may not be used to take wildlife on public land during the period beginning on July 31 and ending on December 31.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-307(4)(c): A trail camera is prohibited on public land during the period beginning on July 31 and ending on December 31, except for use by:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-307(4)(c)(i): the division for monitoring or research;

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-311(2)(c): a class B misdemeanor if the aggregate point value of the protected wildlife determined by the point values established in Subsection (3) is 250 points or less.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-312 Restitution -- Disposition of money.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-312(1): When a person is adjudged guilty of illegal taking, illegal possession, or wanton destruction of protected wildlife, other than a trophy animal, the court may order the defendant to pay restitution:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-312(1)(a): as set forth in Subsection (2); or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-312(1)(b): in a greater or lesser amount than the amount established in Subsection (2).

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-312(2)(a)(i): bison;

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-312(2)(a)(iii): rocky mountain goat;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-312(2)(a)(iv): moose;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-312(2)(a)(v): bear;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-312(2)(a)(vi): peregrine falcon;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-312(2)(a)(vii): bald eagle; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-312(2)(a)(viii): endangered species;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-312(2)(b): $1,250 per animal for:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-312(2)(b)(i): elk; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-312(2)(b)(ii): threatened species;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-312(2)(c): $750 per animal for:

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317 Posted property -- Hunting by permission -- Entry on private land while hunting or fishing -- Violations -- Penalty -- Prohibitions inapplicable to officers.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(1)(a): "Cultivated land" means land that is readily identifiable as:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(1)(a)(i): land whose soil is loosened or broken up for the raising of crops;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(1)(a)(ii): land used for the raising of crops; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(1)(a)(iii): pasturage which is artificially irrigated.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(1)(b): "Permission" means documented authorization from the owner or person in charge to enter upon private land that is either cultivated or properly posted, and shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(1)(b)(i): the signature of the owner or person in charge;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(1)(b)(ii): the name of the person being given permission;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(1)(b)(iii): the appropriate dates; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(1)(b)(iv): a general description of the property.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(1)(c): "Properly posted" means that signs prohibiting trespass or bright yellow, bright orange, or fluorescent paint are clearly displayed:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(1)(c)(i): at the corners, fishing streams crossing property lines, roads, gates, and rights-of-way entering the land; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(1)(c)(ii): in a manner that would reasonably be expected to be seen by a person in the area.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(2): 23A-6-402
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(2)(a): While taking wildlife or engaging in wildlife related activities, a person may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(2)(a)(i): without permission, enter upon privately owned land that is cultivated or properly posted;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(2)(a)(ii): enter or remain on privately owned land if the person has notice to not enter or remain on the privately owned land; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(2)(a)(iii): obstruct an entrance or exit to private property.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(2)(b): A person has notice to not enter or remain on privately owned land if:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(2)(b)(i): the person is directed to not enter or remain on the land by:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(2)(b)(i)(A): the owner of the land;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(2)(b)(i)(B): the owner's employee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(2)(b)(i)(C): a person with apparent authority to act for the owner; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(2)(b)(ii): the land is fenced or otherwise enclosed in a manner that a reasonable person would recognize as intended to exclude intruders.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(2)(c): The division shall provide "hunting by permission cards" to a landowner upon the landowner's request.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(2)(d): 23A-6-402 A person may not post:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(2)(d)(i): private property the person does not own or legally control; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(2)(d)(ii): 23A-6-402 land that is open to the public as provided by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(3): 23A-5-301 A person who violates Subsection (2)(a) or (d) is subject to the penalty provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(4)(a): A person convicted of violating Subsection (2)(a) may have the person's license, tag, certificate of registration, or permit, relating to the activity engaged in at the time of the violation, revoked by a hearing officer.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(4)(b): A hearing officer may construe a subsequent conviction that occurs within a five-year period as a flagrant violation and may prohibit the person from obtaining a new license, tag, certificate of registration, or permit for a period of up to five years.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(5): Subsection (2)(a) does not apply to peace or conservation officers in the performance of their duties.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(6)(a): The division shall provide information regarding owners' rights and duties:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(6)(a)(i): to anyone holding a license, certificate of registration, tag, or permit to take wildlife; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(6)(a)(ii): by using the public media and other sources.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(6)(b): The Wildlife Board shall state restrictions in this section relating to trespassing in the hunting and fishing proclamations issued by the Wildlife Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(7): 77-38b-205 In addition to an order for restitution under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(7)(a): the greater of:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(7)(a)(i): statutory damages in the amount of three times the value of damages resulting from the violation of Subsection (2)(a) or (d); or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(7)(a)(ii): $500; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(7)(b): reasonable attorney fees not to exceed $250, and court costs.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-5-317(8): Civil damages under Subsection (7) may be collected in a separate action by the property owner or the property owner's assignee.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 23A - Chapter 6 - Lands and Waters for Wildlife Purposes
************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-101  Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-101 (1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-101 (1)(a): "General plan" means a document that a municipality or county adopts that sets forth general guidelines for proposed future development of the land within the municipality or county.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-101 (1)(b): "General plan" includes what is commonly referred to as a "master plan."
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-101 (2): "Management plan" means a document prepared in accordance with this chapter that describes how one or more tracts of land owned or managed by the division are to be used.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-101 (3): "Wildlife management area" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-101 (3)(a): a single tract of land owned or managed by the division; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-101 (3)(b): two or more tracts of land owned or managed by the division that are within close proximity of each other and managed as a single unit.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-201 Acquisition of lands, waters, and rights-of-way -- Authority of division.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The division may acquire lands, waters, and rights-of-way by purchase, lease, agreement, gift, exchange, contribution, or any other lawful means, for authorized activities of the division as outlined by this title and the rules made by the Wildlife Board in accordance with

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202 Acquisition of real property held in private ownership -- Published notice and governor's approval required.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(1): 45-1-101 The division may not acquire title to real property held in private ownership without first:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(1)(a): 45-1-101 publishing a notice of the proposed acquisition:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(1)(a)(i): in a newspaper of general circulation in the county in which the property is located; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(1)(a)(ii): 45-1-101 as required in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(1)(b): obtaining the approval of the governor.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(2): (1) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(3): In the case of a proposed purchase of private property, the division may publish notice after earnest money is paid.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(4): The published notice shall inform the public regarding:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(4)(a): the proposed use of the real property;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(4)(b): any conditions on the acquisition of the real property placed by donors, the federal government, sellers, or others specifying how the real property is to be used;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(4)(c): any changes to existing land uses that are anticipated; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(4)(d): the public comment submission process for comments on the proposed acquisition.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(5): The governor shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(5)(a): submit a notification of the proposed acquisition to:

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(5)(a)(ii): the legislators of the legislative districts in which the real property is located; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(5)(a)(iii): the School and Institutional Trust Lands Administration; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(5)(b): invite those notified to submit comments on the proposed acquisition.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(6): After considering comments on the proposed acquisition, the governor may:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(6)(a): approve the acquisition in whole or in part; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-202(6)(b): disapprove the acquisition.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-203(1): Before the purchase of real property held in private ownership, the division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-203(1)(a): first submit the proposition to the county legislative body in a regular open public meeting in the county where the real property is located; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-203(1)(b): by contractual agreement with the county legislative body, approved by the executive director, agree to pay an amount of money in lieu of property taxes to the county.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-203(2): The division shall, by contractual agreement with the county legislative body in which real property previously acquired from private ownership and now owned by the division is located, agree to pay annually an amount of money in lieu of wildlife resource fine money, previously paid to the county.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-203(3): A payment provided for in this section may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-203(3)(a): exceed what the regularly assessed real property taxes would be if the real property had remained in private ownership; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-203(3)(b): include an amount for buildings, installations, fixtures, improvements or personal property located upon the real property or for those acquired, constructed, or placed by the division after the division acquires the real property.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-204 Acquisition of lands by United States for migratory bird refuges.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-204(1): (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-204(1)(a): The state consents to acquisition by the United States of the areas of land or water in the state, as the United States may consider necessary, by and with the consent of the county legislative body of the county where the land or water are located and after approval of application, subject to the laws of the state for water rights, for the establishment and maintenance of migratory waterfowl refuges in accordance with and for the purpose of the Migratory Bird Conservation Act, 16 U.S.C. Sec. 715 to 715s, as amended, and Migratory Bird Hunting Stamp Act, 16 U.S.C. Sec. 718a to 718k, as amended.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-204(1)(b): (1) The United States may use the land or water described in this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-204(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-204(2)(a): This section may not be construed to impose upon the state or an agency of the state an obligation to convey to the United States any interest in land or water owned or controlled by the state, except upon appropriate terms and for adequate consideration.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-204(2)(b): The reservation to the state of coal and other minerals in lands sold by the state within areas so established and easements retained by the state to prospect for, mine, and remove the same are declared to be subject to rules and regulations prescribed from time to time by the Secretary of the Interior for the occupation, use, operation, protection, and administration of these areas as refuges for migratory birds.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-205 Wildlife Land and Water Acquisition Program.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-205(1): (2) As used in this section, "program" means the Wildlife Land and Water Acquisition Program created in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-205(2): There is created a program known as the "Wildlife Land and Water Acquisition Program" under which the division may lease or acquire land or water assets that achieve one or more of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-205(2)(a): protect and enhance wildlife populations;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-205(2)(b): provide the public the opportunity to hunt, trap, or fish; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-205(2)(c): conserve, protect, and enhance wildlife habitat.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-205(3): 23A-6-301; (3)(c) In making a decision as to whether to lease or acquire land or water assets, the division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-205(3)(a): consult the relevant state or county resource management plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-205(3)(b): prioritize leases or acquisitions that involve land that:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-205(3)(b)(i): is adjacent to land already owned by the division; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-205(3)(b)(ii): provides access to other public land;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-205(3)(c): 23A-6-301 develop a management plan for the land or water asset in a manner consistent with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-205(3)(d): (3)(c) facilitate grazing as a management tool if consistent with the management plan described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-205(4): The division shall annually report to the Natural Resources, Agriculture, and Environmental Quality Appropriations Subcommittee regarding how the division expends money in the program.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-301 Management plans.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-301(1): The division shall prepare a management plan for each wildlife management area.  Upon adoption of a management plan by the director, the division shall manage the lands within the wildlife management area in accordance with the management plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-301(2): A management plan shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-301(2)(a): a statement of the proposed or anticipated uses;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-301(2)(b): a description of management limitations or conditions covering the wildlife management area;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-301(2)(c): an inventory of the existing conditions;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-301(2)(d): a statement of the desired future condition of the wildlife management area;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-301(2)(e): a list of strategies that may be implemented to achieve the desired future condition; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-301(2)(f): a description of any reallocation of forage, water, or other resource appurtenant to the land within the wildlife management area.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-302 Preparation of management plans -- Participation by interested persons and local and tribal governments -- Compatibility with local government plans and existing rights.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-302(1): The division shall invite persons who may have an interest in how the land in a wildlife management area is managed to participate in the management planning process.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-302(2): Those persons may include:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-302(2)(a): persons who use, or may use, the land in a wildlife management area for:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-302(2)(a)(i): agriculture, mining, or other commercial pursuits;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-302(2)(a)(ii): hunting or fishing;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-302(2)(a)(iii): recreation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-302(2)(a)(iv): other uses;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-302(2)(b): adjacent or nearby landowners or residents; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-302(2)(c): other interested parties.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-302(3): The division shall invite local government officials to participate in the management planning process.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-302(4): In preparing a management plan, the division shall seek to make land uses compatible with:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-302(4)(a): local government general plans and zoning and land use ordinances; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-302(4)(b): existing rights of others within the wildlife management area.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-302(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-302(5)(a): If the land in a wildlife management area is located within or adjacent to tribal lands, the division shall invite tribal government officials to participate in the management planning process.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-302(5)(b): Participation by tribal officials in the development of management plans for lands owned by the division does not waive the tribe's sovereignty.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-303 Review and adoption of management plans.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-303(1): 63L-11-401 The division shall submit a draft management plan to the Resource Development Coordinating Committee created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-303(2): The division shall submit a draft management plan and any recommendations received from the Resource Development Coordinating Committee and the Habitat Council to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-303(2)(a): the regional advisory council for the wildlife region in which the lands covered by the management plan are located; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-303(2)(b): the regional advisory council for a wildlife region that may be affected by the management plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-303(3): A regional advisory council reviewing a draft management plan may make recommendations to the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-303(4): The director may adopt the management plan, adopt the management plan with amendments, or reject the management plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-303(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-303(5)(a): At the request of the director or a member of the Wildlife Board, the Wildlife Board may review a management plan to determine whether the plan is consistent with Wildlife Board policies.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-303(5)(b): The director may amend a management plan in accordance with recommendations made by the Wildlife Board.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-304 Procedure to revise a management plan.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-304(1): A person seeking a revision of a management plan may request the regional advisory council in the region where the land in a wildlife management area is located to consider the proposal to revise the management plan.  The regional advisory council shall consider the proposal and advise the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-304(2): 23A-6-302; 23A-6-303 The process specified in Sections


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-305 Change in land use where a management plan is not in effect -- Notification to affected persons -- Compatibility with local government plans.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-305(1): If a management plan has not been adopted by the director for a tract of land owned by the division, the division may not change an existing right to use the land until the division notifies those who may be affected by the change and local government officials.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-305(2): When changing an existing right to use the land, the division shall seek to make uses of division-owned land compatible with local government general plans and zoning and land use ordinances.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404 Unlawful uses and activities on division lands.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(1): Except as authorized by statute, rule, contractual agreement, special use permit, certificate of registration, or public notice, a person may not on division land:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(1)(a): remove, extract, use, consume, or destroy an improvement or cultural or historic resource;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(1)(b): remove, extract, use, consume, or destroy sand, gravel, cinder, ornamental rock, or other common mineral resource, or vegetation resource, except a person may collect for noncommercial uses up to 250 pounds per calendar year of common rock or gravel lying on the surface of the ground;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(1)(c): allow livestock to graze;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(1)(d): remove a plant or portion of a plant for commercial gain purposes;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(1)(e): enter, use, or occupy division land that is posted against entry, use, or occupancy;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(1)(f): enter, use, or occupy division land as part of a group of more than 25 people, except a group may include up to 50 persons if the group consists of extended family members;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(1)(g): enter, use, or occupy division land while engaged in or part of an organized event;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(1)(h): use, occupy, destroy, move, or construct a structure, including a fence, water control device, road, survey and section marker, or sign;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(1)(i): prohibit, prevent, or obstruct public entry on division lands when public entry is authorized by the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(1)(j): attempt to manage or control division lands in a manner inconsistent with division management plans, rules, or policies;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(1)(k): solicit, promote, negotiate, barter, sell, or trade a product or service on, or obtained from, division lands for commercial gain;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(1)(l): park a motor vehicle or trailer or camp for more than 14 consecutive days unless the area is posted for a different duration;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(1)(m): light a fire without taking adequate precaution to prevent spreading of the fire or leave a fire unattended;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(1)(n): use fireworks, an explosive, a poison, a herbicide, an insecticide, or a pesticide;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(1)(o): use a motorized vehicle of any kind except as authorized by declaration, management plan, or posting; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(1)(p): use division lands for a purpose that violates applicable land use restrictions imposed by statute, rule, or by the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(2): A person who unlawfully uses division lands is liable for damages in the amount of:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(2)(a): the value of the resource removed, destroyed, or extracted;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(2)(b): the amount of damage caused; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(2)(c): whichever is greater of:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(2)(c)(i): the value of losses or expenses caused as a result of interference with authorized activities; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(2)(c)(ii): the consideration which would have been charged by the division for use of the land during the period of trespass.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(3): This section does not apply to division employees or division volunteers while acting in the lawful performance of the employees' or volunteers' duties.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-6-404(4): 23A-5-301 Except as otherwise provided by statute, the criminal penalty for a violation of this section is prescribed in Section


Utah Code Annotated - Title 23A - Chapter 7 - Cooperative Wildlife Management Units
***********************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-101 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-101(1): "Cooperative wildlife management unit" means a generally contiguous area of land that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-101(1)(a): open for hunting small game, waterfowl, turkey, or big game; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-101(1)(b): registered in accordance with this chapter and rules of the Wildlife Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-101(2): 23A-7-207 "Cooperative wildlife management unit agent" means a person appointed by a landowner, landowner association, or landowner association operator to perform the functions described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-101(3): "Cooperative wildlife management unit authorization" means a card, label, ticket, or other identifying document authorizing the possessor to hunt small game or waterfowl in a cooperative wildlife management unit.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-101(4): "Cooperative wildlife management unit permit" means a permit authorizing the possessor to hunt turkey, or big game in a cooperative wildlife management unit.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-101(5): "Landowner association" means a landowner or an organization of owners of private lands who operates a cooperative wildlife management unit.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-101(6): "Landowner association operator" means a person designated by a landowner association to operate the cooperative wildlife management unit.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-102 Rulemaking authority of Wildlife Board.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
The Wildlife Board may make and enforce rules applicable to cooperative wildlife management units organized for the hunting of small game, waterfowl, turkey, or big game that in the Wildlife Board's judgment are necessary to administer and enforce this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-103 Purposes of wildlife management units.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
A cooperative wildlife management unit is established to:Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-103(1): provide income to landowners;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-103(2): create satisfying hunting opportunities;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-103(3): increase wildlife resources;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-103(4): provide adequate protection to landowners who open their lands for hunting; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-103(5): provide access to public and private lands for hunting.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-201 Operation by landowner association.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-201(1): A landowner association shall operate a cooperative wildlife management unit as prescribed by this chapter and the rules of the Wildlife Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-201(2): For purposes of this chapter, a landowner association operator may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-201(2)(a): be appointed by the division; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-201(2)(b): be an employee or agent of the division.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-202 Certificate of registration -- Renewal.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-202(1): A landowner association may not establish or operate a cooperative wildlife management unit without first obtaining a certificate of registration from the Wildlife Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-202(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The Wildlife Board may renew annually certificates of registration if the landowner association has previously complied with this chapter and the rules of the Wildlife Board made in accordance with

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-203(2): 23A-2-305(3); (2)
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-203(2)(a): A season date for a cooperative wildlife management unit that provides one buck deer permit or more per every 640 acres shall begin on September 1 and end on October 31.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-203(2)(b): A cooperative wildlife management unit that provides less than one buck deer permit per every 640 acres may select the following season date options:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-203(2)(b)(i): beginning on September 1 and ending on October 31; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-203(2)(b)(ii): beginning on September 11 and ending on November 10.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-204 Permits -- Acreage and lands that may be included -- Posting of boundaries.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-204(1): The division shall provide cooperative wildlife management unit authorizations for hunting small game or waterfowl to the cooperative wildlife management unit, free of charge.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-204(2): At least 50% of the cooperative wildlife management unit authorizations for hunting small game or waterfowl provided to a cooperative wildlife management unit shall be offered for sale to the general public at the times and places designated on the application for a certificate of registration.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-204(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-204(3)(a): A cooperative wildlife management unit organized for hunting small game or waterfowl shall consist of private land.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-204(3)(b): At least 75% of the acreage within the boundaries of a cooperative wildlife management unit organized for the hunting of small game or waterfowl shall be open to hunting by holders of valid authorizations.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-204(4): (4)(b)

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-205 Landowner association to provide comparable hunting opportunities.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A landowner association shall provide a holder of an authorization or permit a comparable hunting opportunity in terms of hunting area and number of days.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-206 Compensation for damage -- Claims.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-206(1): A landowner participating in a cooperative wildlife management unit who incurs damages caused by a hunter on the landowner's land may submit a claim and receive compensation for the claim from money received for cooperative wildlife management unit authorization or permit fees collected by the landowner association.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-206(2): (1) The claims under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-206(2)(a): be paid first and have priority over all other obligations of the landowner association;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-206(2)(b): be reviewed, investigated, and paid by the landowner association; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-206(2)(c): not exceed annual revenues of a cooperative wildlife management unit.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-206(3): A landowner participating in a cooperative wildlife management unit who incurs damages caused by a hunter on the landowner's land may not hold the state liable for compensation.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-207 Agents -- Appointment -- Identification -- Refusal of entry by agent.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-207(1): A landowner association may appoint one or more cooperative wildlife management unit agents to protect private property of the cooperative wildlife management unit.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-207(2): A cooperative wildlife management unit agent shall wear or have in the cooperative wildlife management unit agent's possession a form of identification prescribed by the Wildlife Board that indicates that the individual is a cooperative wildlife management unit agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-207(3): A cooperative wildlife management unit agent may refuse entry into private lands within a cooperative wildlife management unit to any person, except an owner of land within the cooperative wildlife management unit and the landowner's employees, who:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-207(3)(a): does not have in the person's possession a cooperative wildlife management unit authorization or permit;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-207(3)(b): endangers or has endangered human safety;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-207(3)(c): damages or has damaged private property within a cooperative wildlife management unit; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-207(3)(d): fails or has failed to comply with reasonable rules of a landowner association.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-207(4): In performing the functions described in this section, a cooperative wildlife management unit agent shall comply with the relevant laws of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-207(5): Title 53, Chapter 13, Peace Officer Classifications For purposes of this chapter, a cooperative wildlife management unit agent may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-207(5)(a): be appointed by the division or the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-207(5)(b): be an employee or agent of the division;

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-209 Failure to comply with rules and requirements.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A person shall leave private property within a cooperative wildlife management unit immediately, upon request of a landowner, landowner association operator, or cooperative wildlife management unit agent, if that person:Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-209(1): does not have in that person's possession a cooperative wildlife management unit authorization or permit;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-209(2): endangers or has endangered human safety;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-209(3): damages or has damaged private property within a cooperative wildlife management unit; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-209(4): fails or has failed to comply with reasonable rules of a landowner association.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-210 Damage or destruction of property.
------------------------------------------------------------------
A person on the land of another person may not intentionally damage, disarrange, or destroy that person's property.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-7-211 Violation of chapter -- Class B misdemeanor.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Any person who violates this chapter is guilty of a class B misdemeanor, unless another penalty is provided elsewhere in the laws of this state.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-101(2)(a): annual or perennial crops harvested from or on cleared and planted land;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-101(2)(b): perennial orchard trees on cleared and planted land;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-101(2)(c): crop residues that have forage value for livestock; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-101(2)(d): pastures.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-101(3): "Depredation" means an act causing damage or death.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-101(4): 23A-8-402(2) "Depredation mitigation plan" means the plan described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-101(5): "Growing season" means the portion of a year in which local conditions permit normal plant growth.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-101(6): "Livestock" means cattle, sheep, horses, goats, or turkeys.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-101(7): "Management unit" means a prescribed area of contiguous land designated by the division for the purpose of managing a species of big game animal.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-101(8): 23A-8-404 "Mitigation review panel" means the panel created under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-101(12): "Wildlife specialist" means a United States Department of Agriculture, Wildlife Services specialist.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-301 Crop damage by pheasants -- Notice to division -- Damages for destroyed crops -- Limitations -- Appraisal.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-301(1): When pheasants damage cultivated crops on cleared and planted land, the owner of the cultivated crops shall immediately upon discovery of the damage notify the division both orally and in writing.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-301(2): Upon being notified of the damage to cultivated crops, the division shall, as far as possible, control the damage.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-301(3): When pheasants damage or destroy cultivated crops on cleared and planted land, the division may pay to the crop owner for the actual damage not to exceed $200 yearly, if the owner notifies the division of the damage within 48 hours after the damage is discovered.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-301(4): (5) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-301(5): If a provision of this section conflicts with the requirements of the federal Pittman-Robertson Act or the regulations issued under that act, the provisions relating to damage claims are void.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-401 Removal of big game animals doing damage.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
The director may authorize the removal of big game animals when the big game animals are doing actual damage. The division shall sell or otherwise dispose of a big game animal removed pursuant to this section and money derived from the sale of these big game animals shall be placed in the Wildlife Resources Account.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405 Compensation for damage to crops, fences, or irrigation equipment -- Limitations -- Appeals.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(1): The division may provide compensation to claimants for damage caused by big game animals to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(1)(a): cultivated crops on private land;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(1)(b): fences on private land; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(1)(c): irrigation equipment on private land.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(2): To be eligible to receive compensation as provided in this section, the claimant shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(2)(a): notify the division of the damage within 72 hours after the damage is discovered; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(2)(b): allow division personnel reasonable access to the property to verify and alleviate the depredation problem.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(3)(a): The claimant and the division shall make an appraisal of the damage as soon after notification as possible.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(3)(b): In determining damage payment, the division and claimant shall consider:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(3)(b)(i): the extent of damage experienced; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(3)(b)(ii): revenue the landowner derives from:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(3)(b)(ii)(A): participation in a cooperative wildlife management unit;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(3)(b)(ii)(B): use of landowner association permits;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(3)(b)(ii)(C): use of mitigation permits; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(3)(b)(ii)(D): charging for hunter access.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(3)(c): The division and claimant may not include speculative damages or claims of future value in an appraisal or damage payment beyond the growing season when the damage occurred under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(3)(d): In determining how to assess and compensate for damages to cultivated crops, the division shall base the division's determination on the:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(3)(d)(i): estimated number of big game animals that damaged or consumed cultivated crops;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(3)(d)(ii): estimated quantity of cultivated crops damaged or consumed by big game animals;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(3)(d)(iii): local market value of the cultivated crops that actually have been or will be damaged or consumed by big game animals;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(3)(d)(iv): replacement value of an equivalent aged tree for perennial orchard trees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(3)(d)(v): other documented costs directly incurred by the landowner or lessee because of damage to cultivated crops by big game animals.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(3)(e): If the claimant and the division are unable to agree on a fair and equitable damage payment, the claimant and division shall designate a third party, consisting of one or more persons familiar with the crops, fences, or irrigation equipment and the type of big game animals doing the damage, to appraise the damage.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(4): (3); (3); (4)(a)

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(4)(b): (3); (3)

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(4)(b)(ii): (3) A claim for damage to irrigation equipment may be paid after appraisal of the damage as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(4)(c): (4)(a)

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(4)(c)(i)(A): $1,000 may be paid pursuant to the conditions of this section; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-8-405(4)(c)(i)(B): the amount in excess of $1,000 may not be paid until the total amount of the approved claims of all the claimants and expenses for fencing materials for the fiscal year are determined.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-9-201 Screens or other devices required -- Failure to install after notice a misdemeanor.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-9-201(1): A person may not take water from the state streams, lakes, or reservoirs for power purposes, or for waterworks, without first furnishing and maintaining suitable screens or other devices to prevent fish from entering the power plants, millraces, or waterworks system.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-9-201(2): A screen or other device is to be built and maintained under the direction of the Wildlife Board and at the expense of the owner or operator.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-9-201(3): A person who fails to install a screen or device within 30 days after the Wildlife Board gives notice in writing to install the screen or device is guilty of a class B misdemeanor.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-9-302 Pollution of waters unlawful.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-9-302(1): A person may not pollute waters:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-9-302(1)(a): the Wildlife Board considers necessary for wildlife purposes; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-9-302(1)(b): containing protected aquatic wildlife and stoneflies (Plecoptera), mayflies (Ephemoptera), dragonflies and damsel flies (Odonata), water bugs (Hemiptera), caddis flies (Trichoptera), spongilla flies (Neuroptera), and crustaceans.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-9-302(2): Each day of pollution constitutes a separate offense.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 23A - Chapter 10 - Aquatic Invasive Species Interdiction
************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101(1)(a): "Conveyance" means a terrestrial or aquatic vehicle or a vehicle part that may carry or contain a Dreissena mussel.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101(1)(b): "Conveyance" includes a motor vehicle, a vessel, a motorboat, a sailboat, a personal watercraft, a container, a trailer, a live well, or a bilge area.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101(2): "Decontaminate" means to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101(2)(a): drain and dry non-treated water; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101(2)(b): chemically or thermally treat in accordance with rule.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101(3): "Dreissena mussel" means a mussel of the genus Dreissena at any life stage, including a zebra mussel, a quagga mussel, and Conrad's false mussel.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101(4): "Equipment" means an article, tool, implement, or device capable of carrying or containing:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101(4)(a): water; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101(4)(b): a Dreissena mussel.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101(5): "Facility" means a structure that is located within or adjacent to a water body.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101(6): "Infested water" means a geographic region, water body, facility, or water supply system within or outside the state that the Wildlife Board identifies in rule as carrying or containing a Dreissena mussel.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101(7): 73-18-2 "Vessel" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101(8): "Water body" means natural or impounded surface water, including a stream, river, spring, lake, reservoir, pond, wetland, tank, and fountain.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101(9): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101(9)(a): "Water supply system" means a system that treats, conveys, or distributes water for irrigation, industrial, waste water treatment, or culinary use.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101(9)(b): "Water supply system" includes a pump, canal, ditch, or pipeline.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-101(9)(c): "Water supply system" does not include a water body.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303 Closing a water body, facility, or water supply system.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(1): (6) Except as provided by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(1)(a): the water body, facility, or water supply system closed to a conveyance or equipment;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(1)(b): restricted access by a conveyance or equipment to a water body, facility, or water supply system; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(1)(c): a conveyance or equipment that is removed from or introduced to the water body, facility, or water supply system to be inspected, quarantined, or decontaminated in a manner and for a duration necessary to detect and prevent the infestation of a Dreissena mussel.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(2): (1) If a closure authorized by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(2)(a): provide a written update to the operator of the water body, facility, or water supply system every 10 days on the division's effort to address the Dreissena infestation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(2)(b): post the update on the division's website.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(3)(a): The Wildlife Board shall develop procedures to ensure proper notification of a state, federal, or local agency that is affected by a Dreissena mussel infestation.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(3)(b): The notification shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(3)(b)(i): the reasons for the closure, quarantine, or restriction; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(3)(b)(ii): methods for providing updated information to the agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(4): When deciding the scope, duration, level, and type of restriction or a quarantine or closure location, the director shall consult with the person with the jurisdiction, control, or management responsibility over the water body, facility, or water supply system to avoid or minimize disruption of economic and recreational activity.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(5): (5)(b)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(5)(a): A person that operates a water supply system shall cooperate with the division to implement a measure to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(5)(a)(i): avoid infestation by a Dreissena mussel; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(5)(a)(ii): control or eradicate a Dreissena mussel infestation that may occur in a water supply system.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(5)(b): (5)(b)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(5)(b)(i): If a Dreissena mussel is detected, the water supply system's operator, in cooperation with the division, shall prepare and implement a plan to control or eradicate a Dreissena mussel within the water supply system.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(5)(b)(ii): (5)(b)(i) A plan required by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(5)(b)(ii)(A): method for determining the scope and extent of the infestation;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(5)(b)(ii)(B): method to control or eradicate the Dreissena mussel;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(5)(b)(ii)(C): method to decontaminate the water supply system containing the Dreissena mussel;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(5)(b)(ii)(D): systematic monitoring program to determine a change in the infestation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(5)(b)(ii)(E): requirement to update or revise the plan in conformity with a scientific advance in the method of controlling or eradicating a Dreissena mussel.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(6): (5)
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(6)(a): (5) The division may not close or quarantine a water supply system if the operator has prepared and implemented a plan to control or eradicate a Dreissena mussel in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(6)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(6)(b)(i): The division may require the operator to update a plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-303(6)(b)(ii): If the operator fails to update or revise a plan, the division may close or quarantine the water supply system in accordance with this section.
