Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-501 Aquatic invasive species emergency response plan.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-501(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-501(1)(a): "Committee" means the Natural Resources, Agriculture, and Environment Interim Committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-501(1)(b): "Emergency response plan" means the statewide aquatic invasive species emergency response plan developed by the division in accordance with this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-501(2): The division shall develop a statewide aquatic invasive species emergency response plan to address the potential spread of aquatic invasive species throughout the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-501(3): In developing the emergency response plan, the division shall coordinate with public and private entities that may be necessary or helpful to remediating the potential spread of aquatic invasive species throughout the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-501(4): The emergency response plan shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-501(4)(a): designate the division as the entity that coordinates the implementation of the emergency response plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-501(4)(b): provide for annual review of the emergency response plan by the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-501(4)(c): provide that the emergency response plan may only be implemented if the division detects aquatic invasive species, including Dreissena mussels, at a water body, facility, or water supply system within the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-501(4)(d): define what constitutes a detection of aquatic invasive species at a water body, facility, or water supply system.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-10-501(5): If an event requires the implementation of the emergency response plan, the division shall report on that event and the implementation of the emergency response plan to the committee.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 23A - Chapter 11 - Big Game
*******************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(1): "Big game" includes deer, elk, big horn sheep, moose, mountain goats, pronghorn.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(2)(a): "Big game byproduct" means those parts of the carcass of a lawfully taken big game animal that are listed in Subsections (2)(a)(i) through (ix):
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(2)(a)(i): bones with less than 1/2 inch of attached muscle tissue;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(2)(a)(ii): fat, tendons, ligaments, cartilage, and silverskin with less than 1/2 inch attached muscle tissue;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(2)(a)(iii): muscle tissue damaged by wound channels and within one inch of damaged tissue;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(2)(a)(iv): head;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(2)(a)(v): rib and neck meat on deer, pronghorn, mountain goat, and bighorn sheep;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(2)(a)(vi): antlers and horns;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(2)(a)(vii): legs below the knee and hock;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(2)(a)(viii): internal organs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(2)(a)(ix): hide.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(2)(b): Notwithstanding Subsection (2)(a), "big game byproduct" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(2)(b)(i): brain or brain tissue;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(2)(b)(ii): spine or any part of the spinal column;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(2)(b)(iii): any portion of the carcass of an animal testing positive for chronic wasting disease;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(2)(b)(iv): any carcass or portion of a carcass that otherwise fails to meet local, state, or federal regulations governing processing, sale, or distribution of wild game; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(2)(b)(v): spoiled product.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(3)(a): "Centerfire rifle hunt" means a hunt for which a hunter may use a centerfire rifle, except as provided in Subsection (3)(b).
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(3)(b): "Centerfire rifle hunt" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(3)(b)(i): a bighorn sheep hunt;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(3)(b)(ii): a mountain goat hunt;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(3)(b)(iii): a bison hunt;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(3)(b)(iv): a moose hunt;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(3)(b)(v): a hunt requiring the hunter to possess a statewide conservation permit; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(3)(b)(vi): a hunt requiring the hunter to possess a statewide sportsman permit.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(4): "Cultivated crops" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(4)(a): annual or perennial crops harvested from or on cleared and planted land;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(4)(b): perennial orchard trees on cleared and planted land;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(4)(c): crop residues that have forage value for livestock; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(4)(d): pastures.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(5): "Financial advantage" means an act through which a person in lawful possession of a protected wildlife carcass uses or disposes of that carcass or carcass parts in a transaction for which the person receives consideration or expects to recover associated costs.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(6): "Management unit" means a prescribed area of contiguous land designated by the division for the purpose of managing a species of big game animal.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(7): "Predator" means a cougar, bear, or coyote.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(8): "Shed antler" means any portion of an antler that:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(8)(a): has been dropped naturally from a big game animal as part of the big game animal's annual life cycle; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(8)(b): has a rounded base commonly known as the antler button or burr attached which signifies a natural life cycle process.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(9): "Shed horn" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(9)(a): the sheath from a pronghorn that has been dropped naturally as part of the animal's annual life cycle; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(9)(b): bighorn sheep, mountain goat, or bison horn naturally detached from the horn core.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(10): "Spoiled product" means any portion of a protected wildlife carcass that is not fit for human or animal consumption due to the presence of parasites, pathogens, or rot.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(11): "Statewide conservation permit" means a permit:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(11)(a): issued by the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(11)(b): distributed through a nonprofit organization founded for the purpose of promoting wildlife conservation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(11)(c): valid:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(11)(c)(i): on open hunting units statewide; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(11)(c)(ii): for the species of big game and time period designated by the Wildlife Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(12): "Statewide sportsman permit" means a permit:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(12)(a): issued by the division through a public draw; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(12)(b): valid:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(12)(b)(i): on open hunting units statewide; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-101(12)(b)(ii): for the species of big game and time period designated by the Wildlife Board.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-202 Commencement date of general rifle deer season.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The general rifle deer season may not commence each year before October 1.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-203 Big game baiting prohibited.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-203(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-203(1)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-203(1)(a)(i): "Bait" means intentionally placing food or nutrient substances to manipulate the behavior of wildlife for the purpose of taking or attempting to take big game.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-203(1)(a)(ii): "Bait" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-203(1)(a)(ii)(A): the use of salt, mineral blocks, or other commonly used types of livestock supplements placed in the field by agricultural producers for normal agricultural purposes; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-203(1)(a)(ii)(B): standing crops, natural vegetation, harvested croplands, or lands or areas where seeds or grains have been scattered solely as the result of a normal agricultural planting, harvesting, post-harvest manipulation, or normal soil stabilization practice.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-203(1)(b): "Baited area" means land within a 50-yard radius of the site where bait is placed, including the site where bait is placed.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-203(2): Unless authorized by a certificate of registration, a person may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-203(2)(a): bait big game;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-203(2)(b): take big game in a baited area; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-203(2)(c): take big game that has been lured to or is traveling from a baited area.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-203(3): The division may only issue a certificate of registration to allow for the baiting of big game if the division determines that baiting is necessary to:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-203(3)(a): alleviate substantial big game depredation on cultivated crops; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-203(3)(b): facilitate the removal of deer causing property damage within cities or towns.

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-204(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-204(1)(a): "Compensate" or "compensated" means anything of value in excess of $25 that is paid, loaned, given, granted, donated, or transferred to a person for or in consideration of locating or monitoring the location of big game animals.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-204(1)(b): "Retain" or "retained" means a written or oral agreement for the delivery of outfitting services or hunting guide services between an outfitter or hunting guide and the recipient of those services.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-204(3)(e): the retained outfitter or hunting guide uses no more than one compensated individual in locating or monitoring the location of big game animals on public land.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-204(4): A registered outfitter or registered hunting guide in good standing may compensate another person to locate or monitor the location of big game animals on public land if:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-204(4)(a): the outfitter or hunting guide has been retained by the recipient of the outfitting services or hunting guide services to assist the recipient take a big game animal on public land;

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-205 Requirement to wear hunter orange -- Exceptions -- Nonhunters.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-205(1): An individual while hunting a species of big game shall wear, on the exterior so the item can be seen, one or more of the following items that are primarily hunter orange material, except as provided in Subsection (2):
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-205(1)(a): a hat;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-205(1)(b): a shirt;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-205(1)(c): a jacket;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-205(1)(d): a coat;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-205(1)(e): a vest; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-205(1)(f): a sweater.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-205(2): An individual is not required to wear a hunter orange item described in Subsection (1):
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-205(2)(a): during the following types of hunts, unless a centerfire rifle hunt is in progress in the same area:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-205(2)(a)(i): archery;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-205(2)(a)(ii): muzzle-loader;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-205(2)(a)(iii): mountain goat;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-205(2)(a)(iv): bighorn sheep;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-205(2)(a)(v): bison; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-205(2)(a)(vi): moose; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-205(2)(b): as provided by a rule of the Wildlife Board made in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-205(3):

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-301 Deer and elk management plans -- Division to confer with others -- Target herd size objectives.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-301(1): The division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-301(1)(a): prepare a management plan for each deer and elk herd unit in the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-301(1)(b): submit the plans to the Wildlife Board for the Wildlife Board's approval.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-301(2): Upon approval of a plan by the Wildlife Board, the division shall manage the herd unit in accordance with the management plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-301(3): In preparing a management plan, the division shall confer with federal and state land managers, private landowners, sportsmen, and ranchers.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-301(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-301(4)(a): A management plan shall establish target herd size objectives.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-301(4)(b): In establishing target herd size objectives, the division and Wildlife Board shall among other factors:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-301(4)(b)(i): consider available information on each unit's range carrying capacity and ownership; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-301(4)(b)(ii): seek to balance relevant multiple uses for the range.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-301(5): Until a management plan for a herd unit is prepared in accordance with this section and approved by the Wildlife Board, the division shall manage the herd unit to maintain the herd size as range conditions and available data dictate.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-301(6): (3); (4) The division or Wildlife Board may revise a management plan as the division or Wildlife Board determines necessary. A revised plan shall be prepared in accordance with Subsections

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502 Big game byproduct -- Certificate of registration.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1): 23A-11-503
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(a): Except as provided in Subsection (1)(f), a person shall obtain a certificate of registration from the division to purchase, acquire, sell, barter, exchange, or trade big game byproduct for financial advantage.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(b): To obtain a certificate of registration authorizing the purchase, sale, barter, or trade of big game byproduct for financial advantage, the applicant shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(b)(i): operate a licensed meat processing business in compliance with state and local government wild game processing laws; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(b)(ii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(b)(ii)(A): provide proof of engagement in the sale of big game byproduct before July 1, 2023, and have processed 500 big game animals in three out of the five consecutive calendar years preceding application; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(b)(ii)(B): have processed 800 big game animals in three out of the five consecutive calendar years preceding application.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c): 23A-11-503 A person receiving a certificate of registration under this section shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(i): post signage in a conspicuous location of the person's business indicating the person's involvement in the program regulated by this section;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(ii): test incoming deer, elk, and moose carcasses from the following areas for chronic wasting disease:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(ii)(A): a state or province, other than Utah, where chronic wasting disease has been detected in big game; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(ii)(B): a management unit within the state that the division has designated as endemic for chronic wasting disease;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(iii): subject to Subsection (1)(d), receive a negative test result for chronic wasting disease before selling, bartering, exchanging, or trading big game byproduct from tested carcasses to another person;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(iv): be subject to reasonable inspections of facilities that process or sell, barter, exchange, or trade big game byproduct and relevant records;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(v): record and upon request of the division, provide the following for a big game animal received:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(v)(A): permit holder's name;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(v)(B): permit holder's phone number;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(v)(C): state or province for which the permit was issued;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(v)(D): permit number;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(v)(E): date animal was received by the processing facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(v)(F): species associated with the permit;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(v)(G): total weight of carcass, in pounds, upon arrival at the processing facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(v)(H): weight of product, in pounds, returned to the hunter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(v)(I): the date the certificate of registration holder submits a deer, elk, or moose carcass for testing for chronic wasting disease;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(vi): retain records detailed in Subsection (1)(c)(v) for two years;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(vii): report to the division the total number of pounds of big game byproduct sold, bartered, exchanged, or traded each fee year on or before the April 15 immediately following the last day of that fee year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(c)(viii): 23A-11-503 at the time the certificate of registration holder submits the report under Subsection (1)(c)(vii), pay a big game byproduct fee in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(d): Notwithstanding Subsection (1)(c)(iii), a certificate of registration holder may sell, barter, exchange, or trade big game byproducts if the big game byproduct is:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(d)(i): not required to be tested under this section; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(d)(ii): required to be tested under this section but a lab result is not provided to the certificate of registration holder within six months from the date the test sample was submitted.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(e): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(e)(i): The certificate of registration holder is responsible for the costs associated with laboratory testing for chronic wasting disease of deer, elk, and moose carcasses from out-of-state hunters, except that the certificate of registration holder may pass the cost of testing to the out-of-state hunter that provides the big game byproduct.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(e)(ii): The division is responsible for the costs associated with laboratory testing for chronic wasting disease for deer, elk, and moose carcasses from hunters within the state, with the costs being paid from the big game byproduct fee collected under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(f): A person may purchase, acquire, sell, barter, exchange, or trade big game byproduct for financial advantage without a certificate of registration, provided the big game byproduct is:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(f)(i): processed and individually packaged for the big game byproduct's intended end use when purchased, acquired, sold, bartered, exchanged, or traded; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(1)(f)(ii): otherwise authorized for purchase, sale, offer or possessed for sale, barter, exchange, or trade by statute or administrative rule.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(2): 23A-5-304 Except as otherwise authorized in this title, rule, or proclamation, a person may not in violation of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(3): A certificate of registration holder agrees to abide by applicable state and federal laws.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-11-502(4): For a carcass testing positive for chronic wasting disease under Subsection (1)(c) and that is surrendered to the division by the hunter, the person named on the certificate of registration under this section may donate unclaimed processed wildlife to the client that is reasonably equivalent in value to the product surrendered to the division.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-12-102 Naming conventions for birds.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-12-102(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-12-102(1)(a): "English-language name" means the name:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-12-102(1)(a)(i): assigned to a bird by a naming entity for use by the English-speaking public; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-12-102(1)(a)(ii): that may differ from the scientific name of the bird.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-12-102(1)(b): "Naming entity" means a nationally recognized entity that maintains a list of official English-language names for birds in North America and South America.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-12-102(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-12-102(2)(a): The division shall use the English-language name assigned to a bird by a naming entity that was in effect on January 1, 2020, when using an English-language name while engaging in the management of the bird or habitat for the bird.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-12-102(2)(b): Notwithstanding Subsection (2)(a), the division may use an English-language name assigned by a naming entity after January 1, 2020, if before January 1, 2020, there was no English-language name.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-12-102(3): The division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-12-102(3)(a): advocate against the changing of eponymous English-language names for birds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-12-102(3)(b): seek the support of national organizations with which the division affiliates to advocate against the changing of eponymous English-language names for birds.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-101 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-101(2)(a): created under this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-101(2)(b): 23A-13-201(1)(b)(iii)(A); (B) used according to the description in Subsections


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201 Creation of a migratory bird production area.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(1)(a): On or before July 1, 2022, an owner or owners of at least 500 contiguous acres of land in an unincorporated area may dedicate the land as a migratory bird production area by filing a notice of dedication with the county recorder of the county in which the land is located.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(1)(b): The notice of dedication shall contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(1)(b)(i): the legal description of the land included within the migratory bird production area;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(1)(b)(ii): the name of the owner or owners of the land included within the migratory bird production area; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(1)(b)(iii): an affidavit signed by each landowner that all of the land, except as provided by Subsection (2), within the migratory bird production area is:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(1)(b)(iii)(A): actively managed for migratory bird:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(1)(b)(iii)(A)(I): production;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(1)(b)(iii)(A)(II): habitat; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(1)(b)(iii)(A)(III): hunting; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(1)(b)(iii)(B): used for a purpose compatible with the purposes described in Subsection (1)(b)(iii)(A).
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(1)(c): A person who files a notice of dedication under this section shall give a copy of the notice of dedication within 10 days of its filing to the legislative body of the county in which the migratory bird production area is located.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(2): 23A-13-302
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(2)(a): 23A-13-302 The notice of dedication may designate land, the amount of which is less than 1% of the total acreage within a migratory bird production area, upon which the landowner may build a structure described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(2)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(2)(b)(i): An owner may build or maintain a road, dike, or water control structure within the migratory bird production area.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(2)(b)(ii): A road, dike, or water control structure is not considered a structure for purposes of Subsection (2)(a).
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(3)(a): Within 30 days of the day on which the county legislative body receives a copy of the notice of dedication under Subsection (1)(c), the county legislative body may bring an action in a court with jurisdiction under Title 78A, Judiciary and Judicial Administration, to cancel or revise a migratory bird production area on the basis that an affidavit filed as part of the notice of dedication under Subsection (1)(b)(iii) is inaccurate.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(3)(b): In bringing the action, the county legislative body shall specify the portion of the migratory bird production area and the affidavit subject to the action.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(3)(c): In an action brought under this Subsection (3), the person who files an affidavit described in Subsection (3)(a) has the burden to prove by a preponderance of the evidence that the affidavit is accurate.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(3)(d): If the court cancels or revises a migratory bird production area, the person who filed the original notice of dedication shall file a revision notice with the county recorder reflecting the court's order.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-201(4): 23A-13-202 In accordance with Section


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-202 Adding to or removing land from a migratory bird production area.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-202(1): Subject to the other provisions of this section, a landowner may file a revision notice with the county recorder of the county in which the migratory bird production area is located to add land to or remove land from a migratory bird production area.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-202(2): The revision notice shall contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-202(2)(a): a legal description of the land added to or removed from the migratory bird production area; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-202(2)(b): the name of the owner or owners of the land added to or removed from the migratory bird production area.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-202(3): A person who files a revision notice under this section shall give a copy of the revision notice within 10 days of its filing to the legislative body of the county in which the migratory bird production area is located.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-202(4): If removing land from a migratory bird production area results in a migratory bird production area of less than 300 contiguous acres:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-202(4)(a): the migratory bird production area ceases to exist; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-202(4)(b): the landowner shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-202(4)(b)(i): notify each landowner within the former migratory bird production area; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-202(4)(b)(ii): file the revision notice required by this section for the entire migratory bird production area.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-202(5): A landowner may add land to a migratory bird production area only if:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-202(5)(a): the land to be added is contiguous to the migratory bird production area; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-202(5)(b): all the landowners of the contiguous land to be added to the migratory bird production area consent to the contiguous land being added to the migratory bird production area.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-202(6): A landowner of a migratory bird production area may include an easement in the migratory bird production area if:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-202(6)(a): the landowner owns the easement;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-202(6)(b): the easement is on land that is contiguous to the migratory bird production area; and
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-202(6)(c): the owner of the land where the easement is located consents to the easement being included in the migratory bird production area.

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-302 Limitations on local regulations.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-302(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-302(1)(a): A county within which a migratory bird production area is located shall encourage the continuity, development, and viability of the migratory bird production area.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-302(1)(b): Except as otherwise specifically provided in this chapter, the purposes, uses, and activities of a migratory bird production area described in this chapter are afforded the highest priority of use status.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-302(1)(c): A structure, improvement, or activity historically or customarily used in conjunction with a migratory bird production area is considered a permitted use under the county's zoning law, ordinance, or regulation.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-302(2): A county within which a migratory bird production area is located may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-302(2)(a): enact a law, ordinance, or regulation that unreasonably restricts an activity normally associated with the migratory bird production area;
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-302(2)(b): change the zoning designation of, or a zoning regulation applying to land within a migratory bird production area unless the county receives written approval for the change from all the landowners within the migratory bird production area; or
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-302(2)(c): enact a law, ordinance, or regulation concerning the use, operation, or discharge of a firearm on a migratory bird production area.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-13-302(3): (2)(a) For purposes of Subsection

It can be anticipated that these uses and activities may now or in the future be conducted on land within the migratory bird production area. Utah Code Annotated - Title 23A - Chapter 15 - Wolf Management Act
******************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-101 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-101(1): "Endangered Species Act" means the Endangered Species Act of 1973, 16 U.S.C. Sec. 1531 et seq.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-101(2): "Service" means the United States Fish and Wildlife Service.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-101(3): "Wolf" means the species Canis lupus.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-102 Legislative findings and declarations.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-102(1): 23A-2-201 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-102(2): The wolf has been listed as endangered under the federal Endangered Species Act throughout the greater portion of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-102(3): The service is the federal agency charged with responsibility to administer the Endangered Species Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-102(4): The service acknowledges that Utah is not critical to the recovery of wolves and that it does not intend to actively recover wolves in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-102(5): The division prepared a wolf management plan outlining the division's management objectives for the wolf in Utah when the wolf was delisted and removed from federal control.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-102(6): The wolf management plan prepared by the division was formally submitted to the service in 2007 for approval.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-102(7): The service has neither approved, denied, nor otherwise commented on the plan since receiving it in 2007.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-102(8): The state formally requested, in writing on multiple occasions, that the service delist the wolf throughout Utah, and the service has failed to acknowledge or otherwise respond to the requests.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-102(9): The state cannot adequately or effectively manage wolves on a pack level in the small area of the state where the species is currently delisted without significantly harming other vital state interests, including livestock and big game populations.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-102(10): It is the policy of the state to legally advocate and facilitate the delisting of wolves in Utah under the Endangered Species Act and to return wolf management authority to the state.


Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-201 Wolf management.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-201(1): The division shall contact the service upon discovering a wolf in an area of the state where wolves are listed as threatened or endangered under the Endangered Species Act and request immediate removal of the animal from the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-201(2): The division shall manage wolves to prevent the establishment of a viable pack in all areas of the state where the wolf is not listed as threatened or endangered under the Endangered Species Act until the wolf is completely delisted under the act and removed from federal control in the entire state.
Utah Code Annotated § 23A-15-201(3): (1); (2) Subsections
